Plans to Improve Transportation Between Japan and Manchuria

(Tokyo) After the completion of the Second Replenishment Plan, the Navy believes that the rich products of Manchuria must be supplied to Japan. Therefore, completing the transportation route across the Sea of Japan is an important preparation for dealing with the 1936 crisis. Therefore, it is currently under study. This transportation route is to develop Tsuruga, Fushiki, Niigata, and the Tsugaru Strait to connect with Rajin and Changchun. The shortest route connecting Niigata with Manchuria and Japan, the time required between Niigata and Changchun is 39 hours, which is 9 hours shorter than via Shimonoseki, 7 hours shorter than via Tsuruga, and 5 hours shorter than via Fushiki. Also, the land in Fushiki is suitable for building factories, so Manchurian products can be quickly transported there, manufactured there, and then distributed to Japan. As for Tsuruga, which has military-related factories, trade can be greatly developed because it controls the Kansai trade area. Also, the Tsugaru Strait is a route through which the United States travels to China and other places, and there are definite hopes for development in the future. Therefore, establishing a new port in the Tsugaru Strait as the gateway from the Pacific Ocean to the Sea of Japan is the most important thing. In addition to the land route, a new air route must be established, as the current air route through Korea requires an overnight stay in the middle, which is very inconvenient. If passing through Niigata, it would only take ten hours to reach Tokyo from Changchun. Therefore, improving the transportation route across the Sea of Japan is indeed necessary for national defense and economic reasons. (Electric News Agency dispatch from the 12th)

Military Faction Recommends Saito Hiroshi as Ambassador to the US

(Tokyo) The Japanese Army Ministry considers the position of Ambassador to the United States to be very important. If the policy towards the US fails, Japan's position in the 1935-36 world conferences will be even more difficult. The Army will recommend Saito Hiroshi, Minister to the Netherlands, for this position. Minister Saito has a reputation as a "hardliner" within the Japanese Foreign Ministry, and is known as part of a group comprised of the former Chief of Intelligence Shiratori and Director of the Asian Bureau Tani, members of the military faction within the Foreign Ministry. Saito was born in Niigata Prefecture in 1886. He graduated from the Faculty of Law of Tokyo Imperial University in 1910 and joined the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. In 1923, he served as Consul General in New York, and has held positions such as Minister to Czechoslovakia, Chief of Intelligence, staff member at the London Conference, Counselor at the British Embassy, and Minister to the Netherlands. He is 48 years old this year, three years older than Shiratori. (China News Agency dispatch from the 12th)

Soviet Russian Government Encourages Immigration to the Far East = Farmers are Exempt from Grain Taxes = Soldiers and Workers Receive Increased Salaries

(Moscow) The Soviet Russian government recently ordered an increase in the salaries of Soviet Russian soldiers and workers in the Far East by 10 to 30 percent. At the same time, it exempted farmers in the Far East from the compulsory delivery of grain for five to ten years, causing a surge in immigration to the Far East. (Reuters dispatch from the 11th)

Taiwanese Aborigines Continue to Resist Japan

Taipei: On the 15th of last month, over forty aborigines from the Taktok tribe in the Daizhu area of the Lilong sub-district of Hualien Port, Taiwan, killed a Japanese policeman named Koasakari and his four children, seized firearms and ammunition, and fled into the mountains. Eighteen of them were recently arrested by the Japanese police, but the others are still resisting together in the mountains. The Japanese police dispatched a large force to encircle and suppress them. However, neighboring aboriginal tribes such as Shinban and Junnu, hearing the news, rose up in succession, built artillery forts, and prepared to resist the Japanese, declaring that they would kill all Japanese soldiers they saw. (China United News Agency dispatch from the 12th)

The Pan American Union's Cooperation with the League of Nations = To Be Discussed at the Next General Assembly

Montevideo: It is heard that US Secretary of State Hull will ask the Pan American Conference tomorrow to adopt a proposal to convene a Pan American Economic Conference in 1934, as proposed by Argentine Foreign Minister Lamas. As for the issue of closer cooperation between the Pan American Union and the League of Nations, it was decided today by a subcommittee meeting to leave it for discussion at the next General Assembly. This action was proposed by US Secretary of State Hull and seconded by five countries: Argentina, Brazil, Chile, Honduras, and Bolivia. The reason given was that the League of Nations had not formally applied to the Pan American Union for cooperation, nor had it sent representatives or observers to attend. This matter was originally proposed solely by Uruguay. (National News dispatch from the 11th)

Regarding Mandated Pacific Islands, Japan is Determined to Possess them Permanently = Even if the League of Nations Is Weak and Does Not Reclaim them, the United States May Not Remain Silent

(Geneva) Today, it was learned from reliable sources that after Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations in 1935, the League of Nations will not take any further action regarding the Pacific islands mandated to it, unless the United States protests. This is because the covenant has not prohibited non-member states from administering former German territories. According to Japanese personnel stationed in Geneva, Japan will retain the islands regardless of whether the League of Nations protests. The reason is that the islands were granted to Japan by the Allied and Associated Powers at the Versailles Peace Conference, so the League of Nations has no right to reclaim them. However, it is anticipated that the United States may not adopt the same attitude as the League of Nations and Japan. The United States is also one of the Allied Powers and can protest Japan's continued administration of the islands after withdrawing from the League of Nations. The United States pays the most attention to the Pacific islands among the Allied Powers because, in the event of a war between Japan and Russia, Japan can use these islands to cut off the traffic between the United States and the Philippines. However, the United States' attitude will still depend on whether Japan has plans to establish fortifications on the islands after withdrawing from the League of Nations. If Japan does so, Washington will protest. (National News dispatch from the 12th)

Executive Yuan Resolution: Appointing Fu Rulin as Vice Minister of Interior, Designating Representatives to the International Labor Conference, and —————————— Abolishing the Mongolian Relief Committee

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan held its 38th meeting on the 12th. Attendees included Wang Zhaoming, Kong Xiangxi, Chen Shuren, Wang Shijie, Chen Shaokuan, Zhu Jiahua, Chen Gongbo, and Shi Qingyang, with Premier Wang chairing the meeting.

(A) Review of Reports: (1) Minister Luo of the Ministry of Judicial Administration, Minister Zhu of the Ministry of Communications, Minister Wang of the Ministry of Education, Vice Minister Gan of the Ministry of Interior, and Director Peng of the Political Affairs Department reported on the review of the "Draft Regulations on Qualification of Qualified County Magistrates under the Registration Law." The review concluded that talents in the provinces of Ningxia, Gansu, Xinjiang, Qinghai, Chahar, and Suiyuan were relatively scarce, and those qualified under the revised regulations for appointing county magistrates were also few. It was proposed to register those who volunteered to serve as county magistrates in the aforementioned provinces and were indeed qualified, as a pilot project. The resolution was passed after review and request for approval.

(B) Resolutions on Appointments and Dismissals: (1) Luo Gonghua, Vice Minister of the Ministry of Interior, was reassigned and should be relieved of his current position. Fu Rulin was appointed as Vice Minister of the Ministry of Interior. (2) Kong Xiangrong was additionally appointed as a member of the Yellow River Conservancy Commission. (3) Minister He of the Ministry of Military Administration submitted the decision of the Military Affairs Commission to additionally appoint Wang Yizhe and He Zhuguo as members of the Beiping Branch, which was approved. (4) The National Government forwarded a request from Kong Xiangxi, Governor of the Central Bank, regarding the terms of office of the bank's supervisors, Li Ming, Yu Hede, Lin Kanghou, Bei Zuyi, Xu Chenmian, and Qin Runqing. According to the regulations of the Central Bank, the terms of office of three of them should be one year, which expired on February 4th. It was requested that they be designated immediately, and that the designated supervisors whose terms had expired be continued in their appointments, in accordance with the regulations. The resolution was to designate Li Ming, Yu Hede, and Lin Kanghou for a one-year term, and to request their reappointment. (5) The National Government forwarded a request from Kong Xiangxi, Governor of the Central Bank, to merge the two Exchange Business Bureaus of the bank into a Business Bureau and to establish a separate National Treasury Bureau. Xi Demao, the original General Manager of the Exchange Business Bureau, should be dismissed. Tang Shoumin, the General Manager of the Business Bureau, requested to resign, which was approved. Xi Demao was appointed as General Manager of the Business Bureau, and Hu Zutong was appointed as General Manager of the National Treasury Bureau. The resolution was passed. (6) Minister Chen of the Ministry of Industry proposed sending Li Pingheng and Xie Dongfa as representatives of the Chinese government to the 18th International Labor Conference, and designating Li Pingheng as the first representative, Bao Huaguo and Luo Shian as government representative advisors, and Zhang Yi and He Jing as government representative secretaries. The resolution was passed.

It was proposed to follow the example of honoring the Sichuan classics expert Liao Ping, and to request the approval of the Executive Yuan to present a commendation, and to separately send Gao's life deeds and academic works to the historical archives, or to be purchased by the state, in order to encourage rare talents and promote the arts. The resolution was passed and communicated to the Legislative Yuan. (4) Chairman Shi of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission reported that the Qinghai Seventh Hutuktu's liaison office in Beijing was proposed to be changed to an office starting from the 23rd year, requesting approval for record-keeping. The resolution was passed. (5) It was resolved to immediately abolish the Mongolian Relief Committee. The Beiping Branch of the Military Affairs Commission and the Political Affairs Reorganization Committee of the Executive Yuan stationed in Beiping were to jointly reassign its staff members as appropriate, provide appropriate subsidies to students, and report the established methods. Yin Tong Arrives in Shanghai from Beijing to Discuss Traffic and Customs Issues

(Nanjing) Yin Tong, Director of the Beining Railway Bureau, left Beijing for Shanghai by night train on the 12th. (Central News Agency, 12th)

(Nanjing) Yin Tong arrived in Beijing on the evening of the 11th and waited to meet Gu Mengyu to report on the administration of the Beining Railway. Yin told reporters on the morning of the 12th that he had drafted several principles for opening the Beining Railway to traffic and submitted them to the Ministry of Railways for review. Previously, negotiations were temporarily suspended due to the lack of agreement on the other party's opinions and various difficulties. The Beining Railway has been built for more than fifty years, with about one-third of the route inside the customs and two-thirds outside the customs. On average, passengers account for one-third and freight accounts for one-third. The railway has been in disrepair for many years, the equipment is simple, and the Luanhe Railway Bridge has long exceeded its insurance period and is quite dangerous. The platforms at the stations along the line are too short, there is a lack of warehouses, and there is no Han Railway Hospital, which urgently needs to be established. Currently, the total monthly income of the railway is about one million yuan, which, after deducting employee salaries, railway debts, and remittances to the Beiping Military Branch for subsidies, leaves little surplus. (Central News Agency, 11th) (Nanjing) Yin Tong also expressed his personal feelings that Chinese people only know how to sing high-pitched tunes and act pretentious, regardless of reality. Since the Incident of September 18th, our country has been singing high-pitched tunes beyond its capabilities, making mistakes again and again, resulting in three mistakes, and ultimately signing the Tanggu Agreement. If we could act according to our capabilities and be pragmatic, why would we completely lose the entire Northeast. The same is true for the various issues of opening traffic and establishing customs. We must not repeat the mistakes of the past, and we must recover one point for every point we can recover, and one foot for every foot we can recover. Recovering one point and one foot will increase our strength by one point and one foot. If we continue to be obsessed with this, the Northeast will never be recovered. He also used a wonderful metaphor for those who oppose opening traffic and mail, believing that it is abandoning the 30 million compatriots in the Northeast: "It is like A having a daughter who is abducted by a robber. A does not try to rescue her, but refuses to recognize her because his daughter has lost her virginity and tainted the family reputation. This is truly unreasonable. The compatriots outside the customs are looking forward to the motherland's rescue every day, but they are completely cut off. This is unbelievable." Yin sighed incessantly. The issue of postal communication has the same reasons as the issue of opening traffic. The people inside the customs consider the Northeast as their hometown, and who doesn't have parents, brothers, wives, and children? Since the suspension of postal communication, it has been impossible to communicate news with their hometowns. The compatriots outside the customs, after being ruled by the violent Japanese, have also been cut off from communication with the interior, and looking to the motherland is like being in another world. What pain is greater than this? However, Japanese and puppet communications are not affected at all. They have already established post offices in Duolun to transmit mail between the Northeast and Inner Mongolia, and are in contact with the puppet post offices in Gubeikou and Yuguan. At the same time, they are also using the method of the interior post offices continuing to send mail on the South Manchuria Railway, so the issue of postal communication must be resolved formally as soon as possible. I have discussed this in detail with Minister Zhu of the Ministry of Communications, and after presenting the urgency of the matter, we are still waiting for a proper solution. The general trend in the future is that we will adopt the method of subsidizing the postage by the recipient, but this needs to be specifically decided by the Ministry of Communications. In short, after September 18th, communication between inside and outside the customs has continued without interruption in terms of telecommunications, but postal communication has been completely cut off, which seems thorough but is not thorough. In name, it is unreasonable, and in fact, it is only misleading ourselves. (Special Dispatch, 12th)

(Nanjing) Yin Tong, Director of the Beining Railway Bureau, intends to submit a traffic plan to Wang and Gu for approval. It is rumored that Wang will submit the proposal to the five ministries of Communications, Railways, Foreign Affairs, Judicial Administration to discuss the principle and review together. (Special Dispatch, 12th)

(Nanjing) A reporter visited Yin Tong and inquired about issues such as the opening of the Beining Railway to traffic. According to him, he had negotiated with the Japanese representatives on several occasions, and had reached the point where the Beining Railway could extend beyond the customs, and the puppet Fengshan Railway vehicles entering the customs should all be changed to the Beining logo. Other ticketing methods had also been discussed to a considerable extent. Subsequently, an order was received from the central government to stop negotiations, so the issue of opening traffic was temporarily suspended. He had also drafted several methods for the issue of opening traffic and submitted them to the central government for review. Once approved by the central government, he would follow the instructions to implement them. Since the governments of the Northeast provinces have not been considered foreign lands, the people of the East provinces are still citizens of the Republic of China. The issue of opening traffic must be realized to facilitate the transportation of compatriots outside the customs. As for the reception of various passes of the Great Wall, it is currently suspended due to an order from the central government. How it will proceed will be in accordance with the orders of the central government. He believes that it is very important to establish customs at the passes of the prepared cities, because our country has not abandoned the land outside the customs, and the people are still engaged in commerce. Establishing customs checkpoints and collecting tax rates to increase financial revenue can be implemented within the principle of not losing power. The central government is currently drafting detailed methods for this, and it should be realized soon. The Japanese are building barracks in Dongluocheng, returning the area to the Suizhong County and organizing a county government. They are also building roads. Since the area is located outside the customs, our country's administrative power cannot reach it, which is very painful. This time, in addition to reporting on matters in North China to Premier Wang, there are several points regarding bureau affairs that need to be reported and discussed with the Ministry of Railways. (Special Dispatch, 12th)

Spain: Slight Turn in the Situation; Socialist Party Rejects General Strike; Fascism to be Implemented Soon; Government Troops Suppress Riots in Disturbed Areas; Insurgent Uprisings Still Occurring Intermittently

Madrid: The political situation in Spain has taken a slight turn. The Socialist Party has refused to support the general strike initiated by the anarchist party, believing that such action would only be exploited by right-wing parties. The authorities now hope that the disturbed areas will soon return to normal. Many believe that the implementation of fascism in Spain is imminent. There was still bloodshed in the disturbed areas today. Two infantry platoons and one militia detachment departed from Valencia, killing two rioters during the suppression of unrest in Teruel, and three militiamen were injured. As government troops were deployed, rioters threw hand grenades, but were driven back by government forces, allowing the troops to advance. Valterrauls declared a Soviet regime, where anarchists killed one militiaman and imprisoned the rest. Troops have now been dispatched from Tarragona to suppress the unrest. Gunfire continued in San Sebastián this morning. A squadron of the cruiser "Fierro" has been ordered to stand by, ready to be deployed to the disturbed areas. Algeciras has declared a general strike, with all ships and trains suspended, cutting off transportation between Spain and Gibraltar. Railway workers in southern Andalusia have also declared a general strike. The express train from Madrid to Seville was stopped today in Los Rosales because local railway staff neglected the train to protest the authorities' arrest of railway workers. The Minister of Interior, fearing a strike by bakery owners in Madrid, has issued a public notice stating that the unrest is gradually subsiding and there is no need to panic. (Reuters, 11th)

Madrid: Although the Spanish government claims to have brought the revolutionary tide under control, the final outcome of the country's political life remains uncertain. Even Spaniards say that no one dares to predict what they will do in this environment. (Reuters, 12th)

No Change in US Monetary Policy; Treasury Secretary Denies Rumors; Senator Pittman's Views on Silver Relief

(New York) Acting Treasury Secretary Morgenthau stated in Washington this afternoon that there has been no change in the Treasury Department's monetary policy. If the Federal Reserve Bank and foreign central banks were indeed in contact, he would be aware of it. Recently, there have been widespread rumors that the Federal Reserve Bank is in contact with the Bank of England and the Bank of France to discuss a method for stabilizing currencies, and that the US government has decided on a fixed gold dollar exchange rate. Today's statement by the Acting Treasury Secretary is intended to dispel these rumors. (Reuters, 11th)

(Washington) Senator Pittman stated today that unless the President takes concrete action to relieve the silver market, Congress will be filled with proposals to re-monetize silver. He intends to propose that all newly mined silver in the United States be minted into coins at a ratio of sixteen to one of silver to gold, estimating that 30 million silver dollars can be minted annually. This is a moderate inflation of currency based on sound coinage. While its effects may be slight and not seen for several years, its true value lies in other silver-producing countries following suit, allowing silver to regain its status as a global currency. (National Telegram, 12th)

Recent Situation in Shanhaiguan

Foreigners Pessimistic that Shanhaiguan Will No Longer Belong to China; The Convenient Import of Narcotics into North China by Manchukuo. A Shanhaiguan dispatch, December 4, in the North China Daily News says: The Manchukuo flag is still flying high over the city of Shanhaiguan. Although there has been much talk recently about the return of Shanhaiguan to China, there have been no major changes in the situation here. The Manchukuo flag is visible everywhere. The roads to the railway station and the traffic station are still guarded by Manchukuo military police. Chinese customs authorities have no power to interfere with incoming and outgoing goods. Therefore, the city is still under the control of the Japanese (Manchukuo) authorities, just as it was in the past. Since the signing of the Tanggu Truce, negotiations for the return of Shanhaiguan have begun. Not long ago, a semi-official source in Dalian announced that the Japanese army was preparing to abandon the key of Shanhaiguan and the long and dangerous line of the Great Wall, which surprised the world. At the time, the public speculated that Japan had been forced to do so by recent developments in international politics. Therefore, the true situation in Shanhaiguan should be of interest to the world, and a brief account is given below.

Since the Japanese army occupied the city in January of this year, it has stationed a brigade of troops in the city. Recently, the number of Japanese troops occupying areas inside the pass has indeed decreased, but there is no sign that they are preparing to return Shanhaiguan. In other words, the reduction of Japanese troops is only the only sign that Manchukuo is reportedly preparing to negotiate the return of Shanhaiguan. The negotiations on the Japanese side are actually handled by representatives appointed by the Kwantung Army, that is, representatives of Manchukuo. They claim to be only dealing with representatives of the Nanjing government regarding the actual situation of negotiations in Beiping, which is extremely difficult to ascertain. However, judging from various pieces of evidence, the main obstacle to a formal return is that the Chinese authorities refuse to negotiate directly with Manchukuo. Although the Chinese authorities are willing to meet with the Japanese at the negotiating table, they are unwilling to conduct public negotiations with the Manchukuo representatives appointed by the Kwantung Army on the takeover of Shanhaiguan and the areas occupied by Japanese troops in the vicinity. At the same time, the status of Shanhaiguan is also very chaotic. Hardliners among the Japanese openly declare that Shanhaiguan is a part of Manchukuo. In fact, the administration of the city, although nominally autonomous, is indeed completely controlled by the Manchukuo authorities. The more moderate Japanese claim that Shanhaiguan is only temporarily occupied by the Japanese army and that the city is now practicing self-government. As for the so-called self-government, the administration of Shanhaiguan is now managed by Chinese officials elected by the local (citizens). These Chinese officials are all appointed by the Japanese, and the elections are merely a facade. Therefore, it is difficult to say that the administration of Shanhaiguan is truly independent. Now, the three issues of through-trains, customs duties, and postal services are being contested by both sides, and it is difficult to resolve them for a while. It is said that Manchukuo insists on opening Shanhaiguan as a free port, so that Manchukuo's drug cartels can import narcotics into North China with great convenience. A Manchukuo customs office has now been built between the railway station and the city of Shanhaiguan. It is said that Manchukuo is also planning to build housing for its customs personnel, and temporary barracks are being hastily built about one mile outside the east gate to accommodate the Kwantung Army, which is said to be able to accommodate 1,500 people. Therefore, even if Shanhaiguan is returned to China, military encroachment will remain forever. It is also rumored that the Japanese are planning to build a new city near these barracks. This news has made the Chinese and residents very uneasy, because if it is realized, it will add to the coercion. However, according to the opinions of foreigners, this is deliberately spread by the Japanese to intimidate the local Chinese, so that they will firmly oppose changing the current status of Shanhaiguan, so as to prevent the Japanese and Manchus from abandoning Shanhaiguan and building a free port opposite the city to seize the trade on which Shanhaiguan relies for its survival today. Free trade is indeed sufficient to help Shanhaiguan's development. Judging from the phenomena, the final solution to the current stalemate is to make Shanhaiguan an autonomous city, enjoying the special benefits of a free port. As for the administration, it will be presided over by the Chinese, to save the face of He and Huang of Beiping. At the same time, the Chinese customs can set up customs offices on the border of the free port to stop the source of drugs from flowing into North China. This is the general view of the Chinese and Japanese in this area, but foreigners are all pessimistic and see Shanhaiguan as never again belonging to China.

Eastern Guangdong: Defensive Works Constructed Everywhere; Large Armies Gather in the Upper Reaches of the East, Han, and Liang Rivers

A Shantou dispatch from Li Yangjing's military conference in Meizhou states that after the Fujian Incident, rumors spread throughout the Guangdong-Fujian border area. The counties of Chaozhou and Meizhou have been under winter defense martial law since the first of the month. Shantou police are also fully armed on patrol. After 10 p.m., there are few pedestrians on the streets. All ships entering and leaving Shantou Port are limited to between 6 a.m. and 6 p.m. No traffic is allowed after that time. A Japanese warship entered and docked in the waters off Qilu on the afternoon of the 5th. Although rumors are rife in Chaozhou and Shantou, local order in the counties remains good. Trenches and fortifications are everywhere. Solid defensive works have been built on Tiger Head Mountain, where Raoping Huanggang borders Chenghai Donglong. There are pillboxes in every mountain village where Raoping borders Zhian and Pinghe, too many to count. There are also trenches in Maqian, Shangrao, and Shiyun, where Dapu borders Raoping. Guangdong troops are stationed in Yongding Fengshi and Shishang above Dapu. There are trenches everywhere in Jiaoling Wuping, Shanghang, Pingyuan, Xingning, and Xunwu. Since Commander Li Yangjing returned to defend the area, the Third Army headquarters has made many changes to the defense areas of each division at the Meizhou military conference. For example, the original two regiments of the Independent First Division, commanded by Huang Renhuan, were stationed in Shanghang. Because the terrain in that defense area was prominent, they have been withdrawn to Wuping to Yongding Fengshi, shortening the line against Fujian and preventing attacks by the Communist bandits. The Huang Zhiwen Division stationed in Jiangxi has also shortened its line due to the prominence of the defense line, establishing contact with the Huang Renhuan Division. The Huang Yanzhen Division is connected with the Huang Renhuan and Zhang Ruigui divisions. At present, large armies are gathering in the upper reaches of the East, Han, and Liang rivers, actively deploying defenses. All key passes have been dug with trenches. Trenches are everywhere in Chaoan: Zhugaoshan, Bijia, and at the foot of Phoenix Mountain. The long trench from the North Gate Gang of Meixian to Wuliting was originally dug by Jiang Guangnai when he defeated Zhu De and Mao Zedong in Meixian and has been preserved for many years. Now the original trenches have been re-repaired. The long trenches of Dalongtian, Luogang, Niudougang, Shizheng, Bachi in Pingyuan, Wuhua, Anliu, Wujingfu, Huayang, Heshi in Zijin, and Fucheng in Fengshun are the latest and greatest buildings. The trenches are lined up in Luojiayue, Tangkeng, Xinxu, and Huizhai, where Chaoan Fengshun borders. As for the official road between Fengshun and Xingning, such as Houzidong, Qingtan, Xiamuluojing, and Baxiangshan, the terrain is also used everywhere to build fortresses. The Guangdong army's deployment in the eastern region this time is more stringent than ever before. The purpose of Li Yangjing's military conference in Meizhou was to adjust the defense lines of each army and urge the construction of roads. Yang Youmin, chief of staff of the Eastern District Pacification Headquarters, and Li Hua, director of the Highway Bureau, went to Meixian on the 2nd. Yang returned to Shantou on the 6th, while Li stayed in Meixian. In order to urge the early completion of the second, third, fourth, and fifth arterial roads in the eastern district, Li Yangjing accompanied Li Hua and personnel from the military headquarters on an inspection tour of the second arterial road, which runs from the Meisong Road to Dapu and then into Fengshi. The second arterial road runs from Huizhou through Zijin, Wuhua, and Xingning to Songkou in Meixian and has been completed in sections. Only the section from Songkou to Dapu has not been completed. Li's arrival in Meizhou came from the second arterial road. After inspecting the second arterial road, he will inspect the third arterial road from Wuhua Anliu to Fengshun Jieyang, and then inspect the fourth arterial road from Zijin to Xingning Xichang into Pingyuan. Finally, he will inspect the fifth arterial road from Chaoan through Phoenix Mountain into Raoping City and out of Qiandong to Huanggang Zhaoan. Li's inspection is expected to reach Shantou by the end of the month and will personally order the army division commanders stationed in various places to strictly order the soldiers under their command to assist in road construction. Each arterial road is limited to holding a ceremony for the completion of contact traffic with the first arterial road on New Year's Day next January to facilitate military and commercial transportation. (6th)

Jiading: Automobiles Run Between Nanxiang and Shanghai

The highway from Nanxiang to Zhenru was completed by the county Construction Bureau in the previous year, and private cars often traveled back and forth. When Wang Jingwei, President of the Executive Yuan, traveled from Nanjing to Shanghai, he would take the Nanjing-Shanghai train to Nanxiang Station and then take a car to Shanghai via this road. Now, Huang Yangluo, a local resident, and Zhang Yonggao, the owner of an automobile dealership on Baoshan Road in Shanghai, have purchased two provincial highway automobile licenses from the Construction Department. They have established a second branch in Nanxiang and started a trial run of Nanxiang-Shanghai automobiles on the 10th, which proved to be very successful. Therefore, starting on the 13th, they will use two provincial highway license vehicles and ten Shanghai city license vehicles to carry passengers from Xiancha Bridge in Nanxiang to Baoshan Road in Shanghai, with six scheduled trips back and forth. The Shanghai to Nanxiang times are 7:00, 8:00, 11:30 a.m., 3:30, 4:30, and 5:30 p.m. The Nanxiang to Shanghai times are 8:00, 9:00 a.m., 1:00, 4:00, and 5:15 p.m. The fare for each passenger is 40 cents. However, local organizations believe that the road was built with county funds, but now the company is actually using two provincial highway licenses to carry passengers on scheduled trips, actually occupying the entire public road privately, and will make some kind of protest.

Songjiang: Robbery of Four Families in One Night

It is the time of winter defense, and robberies are frequent everywhere. Last night (11th) at about 11 p.m., the home of Shan Wenzhun, the head of Shan Jiaqiao Township, Fourteen Map, outside the south gate, was suddenly broken into by more than ten robbers carrying pistols, while the family was still half-asleep. Three of the robbers threatened with pistols, while the others entered the house and robbed freely. After robbing, they went to the room of Shan Huohai (Wenzhun's uncle), who lived in the same house, broke open boxes and overturned chests, searching for clothes and ornaments. They dragged Huohai to Wenzhun's room and locked him up. The robbers then went to the Qiu family in Xiaojinjing Village, about a hundred steps south. The two households of Yonggen and A-Qiu, brothers, were robbed at the same time. Yonggen's son, A-Xiaogou, heard the alarm and jumped out of the back window to escape to the other side of the river, shouting for the arrest of the robbers. He was heard by the robbers, who shot at him, hitting A-Xiaogou. The bullet entered his back and exited his chest, and his leg was also hit by a bullet. Blood flowed like a river. He was then beaten violently with a tree branch, and A-Xiaogou fainted to the ground. The robbers then carried their loot and left. It is estimated that the four families lost a considerable amount of money. The victims reported the robbery to the police for investigation in the morning. The injured A-Xiaogou was carried to Songjiang Hospital for treatment by his family. It is not known whether his life is in danger.

Refugee Women Come to Songjiang to Raise Funds

Recently, ten young women claiming to be refugees from Jiangxi, dressed neatly, led by a man named Wang Yushan, went to the First Sub-Station of the Public Security Bureau, requesting to raise funds. They said that they had suffered from banditry in Jiangxi and had left their homes to seek a living. They planned to go to Hangzhou but lacked travel expenses, and asked for assistance. The sub-station sent police to monitor them. After the refugees raised funds from merchants, they were escorted out of the area.

Suzhou: A Large Number of Hostages from Zhouzhuang Escape Danger

Tang, the wife of the owner of Yangjia Gang soup shop in Zhouzhuang, and her son, Tiger, as well as Ruan and Shen, the daughters-in-law of Xia Junde in nearby Lujia Gang, and their grandson, A-Xiaomao, were all kidnapped by bandits last month and held for ransom. Because the victims had no money to redeem the tickets, there was no way out. The bandits hid the hostages at the bottom of the bandit boat for more than ten days. The day before yesterday (11th), the bandit boat was parked overnight on the shore of Cheng Lake. In the middle of the night, while the bandits were sound asleep, all the hostages except the small hostage, Tiger, who was fast asleep and did not wake up, took the opportunity to go ashore and escape. Yesterday (12th), they escaped back to their homes in Zhouzhuang Township. The public security bureau questioned the hostages, asking them about their kidnapping and escape.

Minister Luo Inspects Prisons and Penitentiaries

Minister of Justice Luo Wengan came to Suzhou to inspect the judiciary. After inspecting the High Court and the Third Prison on the (11th), he went to the Railway Hotel to rest because it was already dusk. Yesterday (12th), he continued to inspect the District Court, the Third Prison, and the Penitentiary. He is scheduled to leave Suzhou by train at 9:50 this morning (13th) to go to Wuxi, and then to Zhenjiang and Yangzhou for inspections.

Wuxi: Director of the Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau Caught in Embezzlement

Qiu Jiusheng, the director in charge of collecting tobacco and alcohol taxes in the three counties of Wuxi, Changshu, and Jiangyin, has been repeatedly accused of wrongdoing. After the General Taxation Department sent personnel to investigate, they found that Qiu had indeed embezzled funds. He was immediately dismissed from his post and handed over to the Wuxi County Government for detention. His vacancy was filled by Qin Jianyuan, a native of Wuxi, who took over the job the day before yesterday. Qin is the son of Qin Yuzhao, the former magistrate of Wuxi County, and was previously the secretary of the Zhongnan Bank.

Nantong: Gu Renfa Secretly Investigates in Nantong

Two visitors from Zhenjiang arrived at the Youfei Hotel in Chengnan on the 10th. In the guest register, they wrote that their names were Gu Minyu, 36 years old from Guangdong, and Zhao Yuxin, 30 years old from Henan. Both said they were visiting friends in Nantong and brought two Shandong servants with them. The hotel asked for a guarantor, so they filled in Fu Qianzhi, who is said to be the new director of the Nantong County Public Security Bureau. However, he has not yet taken office and is staying at the club. The Public Security Bureau's supervisory office checked the rooms in the evening and especially instructed that Gu and Zhao were from the province and should be kept secret. Therefore, it is rumored that Gu Minyu is an alias for Gu Renfa. Gu's actions are extremely secretive, and he refuses to see visitors. He went out early in the morning on the 11th, and it is not known where he went. At 6 p.m., Zhao Yuxin borrowed two plainclothes armed patrol officers, Jiang Zhiping and others, from the urban public security branch, and accompanied them to Chuan Gang on the border of Tonghai in a car, saying they were handling a case.

Changzhou: The Department Orders Strict Investigation of Overcharges for Construction Donations

Meat merchants' representatives Zhang Zhongdao and Wu Wenyuan of Wuyi have repeatedly filed complaints with the Provincial Department, accusing Qiu Youhe, Zhang Xuanxin, and others of embezzling construction special donations collected from slaughter taxes, amounting to more than 10,000 yuan. The Provincial Department has repeatedly ordered the county to investigate, but former County Magistrate Zhang's reply seemed to indicate a misunderstanding. Since the reorganization of the Provincial Government, Zhang Zhongdao and others have again filed a complaint with the Provincial Government, attaching certificates and other evidence, requesting that a fair and competent person be quickly selected to supervise the meat merchants, adjust and verify the accounts, and strictly pursue and limit the payment. The Financial and Construction Departments have jointly ordered a strict investigation. The Construction Department has sent Chen Heng'an and the Finance Department has sent Lu Fengtai, the director of the Wujin business tax bureau, to the county government to take the case files filed by Zhang Zhongdao and others, collect the slaughter tax collection records and special construction donations accounts for the past years, and summon the original defendants and witnesses to the county for a thorough investigation. If the accusations are found to be true, the defendants will be detained by the county government to recover the money. Chen Heng'an and others arrived in Changzhou on the 12th and are working with County Magistrate Cai and Lu Fengtai to investigate the truth of the case before submitting a report.

Jiangyin: Headquarters Order: No Visits to Forts Allowed

The General Staff Headquarters considers fortress areas to be vital to national defense and military affairs. Therefore, visits by all persons, both Chinese and foreign, should be strictly prohibited to prevent leaks that could lead to miscalculations in military operations. The General Staff Headquarters recently received a report from Staff Officer Liu Tianfu and Adjutant Xie Youan that during their inspection of Jiangyin, personnel from other organizations were observed visiting the newly built forts. The General Staff Headquarters specifically ordered Commander Xie that the fortress area should be implemented in accordance with the Law on Fortress and Fortified Zone Areas. Regardless of whether the buildings are new or old, visits by the public are prohibited. Even if local officials and gentry request visits, they should be handled in accordance with the Area Law.

[P Yangzhou: Ministry's Response to the Yutong Relocation Case

The Jiangdu County Chamber of Commerce, due to the Yutong relocation case, together with the Agricultural Education Law Firm and the Reporters Association, jointly sent telegrams to the Provincial Government, the Ministry of Finance, and the Salt Commissioner's Office, requesting a halt to the relocation. Now, in addition to receiving a provincial approval stating that the Ministry of Finance has been instructed to order the transport commissioner to strictly prohibit the relocation, the chambers of commerce were notified on the 11th that a decree was received from the Ministry of Finance on the 9th, stating in brief that the telegrams and the Salt Commissioner's Office's report to the Chamber of Commerce, etc., have been received. After investigation, the Yutong salt production area was originally located in the Chenjiagang area of northern Jiangsu. Since the transport commissioner relocated northward to reorganize the production area, he repeatedly ordered the Jinan companies to relocate their headquarters northward to facilitate local management. Yutong's relocation is being carried out in accordance with the order, but it has been reported that it was approved by a shareholders' meeting. The company's headquarters relocation has no impact on salt transport or embankment work. Other local public, charitable, educational, construction, and business donations will continue as before. The Ministry previously ordered the Huai transport commissioner to comply and informed the chambers of commerce not to worry excessively.

Letter

To the Editor:

I have recently read the Zhenjiang correspondence column in your newspaper of December 1st of this year, which stated that during the three investigations of Hua Zhen, the former magistrate of Xinghua County, the plaintiff made statements that seemed to exonerate Hua, claiming that he was taking the blame for others and requesting that the judge treat Hua leniently. After investigation, the Zhenjiang Court only summoned the plaintiff Wei Chonggeng to court for questioning once. During that hearing, Chonggeng and others made statements based on facts and did not request that the judge treat Hua leniently. Official records are available for verification. Moreover, the court has the power to weigh the severity of the case, so how could Chonggeng and others rashly make such a request? We are concerned that this is inaccurate hearsay. We respectfully request that the editor-in-chief investigate and promptly make corrections. Addressed to the Editor-in-Chief of Shen Bao. From: Wei Chonggeng, Director of the Xinghua County Farmers' Association; Gu Lunan, Chairman of the Xinghua County Chamber of Commerce; Pan Dejun, Standing Director of the Xinghua County Education Association; Zhao Baosen, Standing Director of the Xinghua County Fishermen's Association; Wu Guangguo, Standing Committee Member of the Xinghua County Executive Committee; Zhu Liangfu, Standing Committee Member of the Xinghua Relief Institute Foundation Committee; Zhao Liangbi, Former Standing Committee Member of the Xinghua Storage Committee. December 9th, Year 22.

Local News: Military and Political Authorities Issue Proclamation to Reassure the People

Mayor Wu also made a statement to the Central News Agency, saying that recently the military campaign to suppress bandits in Jiangxi has been making steady progress, while in Fujian Province, there was a sudden act of destroying the Party and betraying the country. Malcontents hope to create disturbances in the middle. Since this city is the pivot of the Southeast, the military and political authorities of this city are taking strict precautions. Mayor of this city and Garrison Commander Wu Tiecheng, has issued an important statement and a proclamation was issued by the Songhu Garrison Headquarters and the Municipal Government, so that all citizens can live and work in peace. The statement of Wu and the proclamation are recorded separately as follows:

Wu's Statement

The military campaign to suppress bandits in Jiangxi is now making steady progress, and it is hoped that it will be completely eradicated soon. The people in our rear areas should also work together to promote this work. As for the rebellion in Fujian Province, the central government will be able to quell it within the shortest possible time. Recently, there have been reactionary elements and speculators who have taken the opportunity to spread rumors to confuse the public, which is hateful. The military and political organs of this city have a duty to not pardon them, and have ordered the military and police organs to strictly investigate. At this time of internal and external troubles, the Chinese people are working hard to survive. Survival requires unity of spirit, support for the central government, and consolidation of unity. Only then will there be hope for the future of the nation and the people.

Joint Proclamation

The Songhu Garrison Headquarters and the Shanghai Municipal Government jointly issued a proclamation yesterday, which stated: In order to issue a proclamation, it has been found that since the suppression of the Communist bandits in Jiangxi Province, there have been successive reports of victories, and the chaos will be quelled soon. Shanghai is the hub of the Southeast and is a major town. At this time of national crisis, the security of the rear should be strengthened so that the military can achieve success as soon as possible. Recently, it has been found that unscrupulous people and reactionary elements are lurking in the city, spreading rumors, and attempting to incite unrest in order to carry out their conspiracies. Their intentions are evil and hateful. In addition to ordering the military and police to strictly investigate and arrest them for prosecution, all citizens must be diligent in their occupations and must not easily believe rumors or disturb each other. This proclamation is hereby issued, and everyone must comply.

With the Minbian (Fujian Incident) not yet resolved, and the anniversary of the Guangzhou Communist Uprising, both the Chinese and foreign concessions were on high alert for the past two days. The Municipal Government has ordered the military and police agencies to step up winter defenses to prevent unforeseen events. The Municipal Government and the Garrison Headquarters have jointly issued a proclamation to strictly investigate reactionaries. Mayor Wu issued a statement urging unity to survive. Details are recorded separately below:

Continued Alert Yesterday

The Municipal Government received confidential reports that the Communist Party members in this city would take the opportunity to cause trouble on the previous two days. The concession areas also sent letters to the authorities concerned to jointly carry out patrols. Passed Peacefully

The city was deserted at night, and the posts in the Chinese and foreign concessions were all doubled, and the defense was very strict, so the past two days have passed peacefully.

Stepped-Up Winter Defense

The Municipal Government also ordered the military and police agencies to be more strict in winter defenses during the Minbian period. Marconi Returns to His Country Yesterday: Lunch at the Italian Consulate to Entertain Italian Nationals in Shanghai: Boards Italian Ship Conte Rosso at 3:00 to Return to Italy

The two ladies representing scientific groups presented flower baskets to Marconi, the Italian inventor of radio. Mr. and Mrs. Marconi have been traveling in the Far East, coming to China from Japan, first to the three northeastern provinces, then to Tianjin and Beijing, and arriving in Shanghai on the 7th. They have been warmly welcomed by all parties in recent days. Yesterday at noon, Mr. Marconi hosted a banquet at the Italian Consulate at 555 Jing'an Temple Road to thank the Italian nationals in Shanghai. After the banquet, at around 2:00, he and Italian Ambassador Botz Cristler drove to the Bund on Nanjing Road, took the consulate's special launch. Those who were present included the Italian Ambassador and his wife, the Italian Consul General Nilon and his wife, the Italian Naval Commander, the General Manager of Marconi Company Leciocci and his wife, the Engineer of the Sino-British International Radio Station Henry, and Mellon, the representatives of the 14 academic groups in Shanghai Fang Ziwei, Cao Zhongyuan, the President of the Italian Chamber of Commerce, the embassy and consulate staff, and Italian nationals. At 3:00, they boarded the Italian ship Conte Rosso. After a short rest, they were entertained in the hall by those who came to see them off. Ms. Chen Shujuan, wife of Fang Ziwei, and Ms. Fang Qian, the fourth daughter of Fang Jiaobo, representing the 14 academic groups in Shanghai, presented Mr. and Mrs. Marconi with two flower baskets. Mr. Marconi bowed and shook hands, expressing his deep gratitude. He said that China is a good place, the people are kind and friendly, and full of emotions, and the young scientists are working hard. The academic development in the future is unlimited. He hopes to have the opportunity to come to China again in the future. At 3:30, the gong rang, and the ship set sail. After shaking hands with the welcomers and saying goodbye, the ship is expected to arrive in Italy around the third of next month. It is heard that Mr. Marconi will disembark for a short visit when the ship passes Hong Kong, and will return to Italy on the original ship.

Japanese Consul Illegally Arrests Jin Xi: Municipal Government Has Lodged Protest

The Taxpayer Association sent a letter to the Municipal Government requesting negotiations to the Central News Agency. The Municipal Government has lodged a protest with the Japanese consul, and no reply has been received yet. However, according to the Japanese consul, Jin Xi is related to the Hongkou assassination case and it is difficult to expect a concrete reply in a short time. The Chinese Taxpayer Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to Mayor Wu yesterday regarding the Jin Xi case, stating: Respectfully, it is reported that the Korean Jin Xi, who had long ago acquired Chinese nationality, was illegally kidnapped and taken away by the Japanese while living in the French Concession. The French Concession authorities allowed the Japanese to infringe upon their police power, and the French consul ignored the violation of international agreements. According to the provisions of international law, even people with dual nationality are subject to the laws of their place of residence. The French Concession is the territory of the Republic of China. Even if Jin Xi had original nationality that has not been lost, according to the agreement of international law, if there is a suspicion of crime, he should be detained and interrogated by the Jiangsu Shanghai Second Special District Local Court. However, Jin Xi was illegally kidnapped by the Japanese, and the police power of the French Concession and the status of the French consul were trampled on. Are the residents in the French Concession at risk of being illegally kidnapped by the Japanese at any time? Is it still possible to maintain legal order? Therefore, we hereby respectfully request that the government promptly conduct serious negotiations with the consuls concerned to recover Jin Xi and restore his freedom in order to protect national sovereignty and maintain legal order in the concession. I am very grateful. This is addressed to the Mayor of Shanghai Municipal Government Wu.

Sino-British Telegraph Soon to Be Connected: = All Machinery Installed = = Current Work on Adjustment and Correction = = Date of Telegraph Connection to be Determined Within the Month =

The International Telecommunications Bureau of the Ministry of Communications believed that the original radio station was insufficient for Sino-British telegraph communication, so it specially built a new transmitting station next to the Zhenru International Radio Station. The entire project was completed as early as the end of August. The four large receivers, two twenty-kilowatt transmitters, and one telephone ordered from the British Marconi Company have all been shipped to Shanghai. The engineers of the station have supervised the workers to transport the four receivers to Liuhe for installation, and the two transmitters and one telephone to the Zhenru Radio Station for installation. The above projects have been completed one after another. The engineers of the station have been actively carrying out correction work and checking whether there are any errors in the installed machines.

Installation of Underground Cables to be Completed by the End of the Month

According to the person in charge of the station, there are telephone antennas installed along the route between the Zhenru Radio Station and the radio station in the Sassoon Building on Nanjing Road in the city. Fearing that the antennas will encounter difficulties in the event of wind, rain, or other unforeseen events, underground cables have been laid along the route from Zhenru to the radio station in the Sassoon Building on Nanjing Road. Since the project started in October, it has been largely completed and will be fully completed by the end of this month.

Additional Motor Installed for Emergency Needs

All the machines in the radio station rely on electricity to operate. The electricity required is currently supplied by the Zhabei Water and Electricity Plant. The amount of electricity used each month is quite large. In order to save expenses and prevent the water and electricity company from having an accident or stopping the supply of electricity, the station purchased a generator from the Construction Committee of the Ministry of Communications in Nanjing and added a house next to the radio station in mid-October to install the motor. The entire project will be completed within a few days. It is also said that the power of the newly installed generator is sufficient to supply all the machines in the radio station.

First Batch of American Wheat Shipped to Shanghai: Delayed Five Days Due to Heavy Fog: Total of 8,940 Tons Loaded

The first batch of American wheat purchased on credit by our country will be imported on Sunday. It was originally scheduled to arrive at the Wusongkou on the 11th and be imported and unloaded on the 12th. Unexpectedly, there has been heavy fog on the sea for days, which has caused a delay of five days to Shanghai. The reporter of this newspaper inquired about the details yesterday, and the details are recorded separately as follows:

Amount Shipped

The first batch of American wheat borrowed was started to be transported and loaded from Portland, North America on November 16 on the British ship Bank Line, which was leased by the China Merchants Bureau, which is the ship of the world-famous Bank Line. The ship set off from the United States on the 20th. The entire ship was loaded with 8,940 tons, totaling about 95,000 bags. According to the usual practice, it should arrive in Shanghai in 14 days. Therefore, the shipowner's report also confirmed that it could be imported at the latest yesterday.

Encountered Heavy Fog

After leaving the United States, the ship was very peaceful along the way. When it was about to reach the territory of Japan, the weather suddenly turned bad, and heavy fog fell on the ocean, making navigation very dangerous. In order to ensure safe navigation, the ship stopped sailing to avoid the fog, and anchored for four consecutive days. It was not until yesterday that the fog cleared that the shipowner telegraphed to Shanghai to start sailing, so it could not arrive in Shanghai for delivery according to the scheduled period.

Imported This Week

Yesterday afternoon, the reporter inquired about the truth from a Westerner and was told the definite news that the Array Fubengk wheel could arrive in Shanghai yesterday morning, but it was blocked by fog and had to be postponed for five days. It will arrive in Shanghai on the 17th. However, the 8,900 tons of American wheat loaded in the ship have been sold to the Hakka people, so there is no need to unload them in the warehouse. As soon as they arrive in Shanghai on Sunday, they can be delivered from the ship's side. The owners have been notified to prepare barges for transshipment at that time.

Coming One After Another

The second and third batches of American wheat have also been handed over to the Stein Company to send two ships, totaling 16,000 tons. The Array Gen will transport 8,000 tons and will be imported on the 23rd of this month. The Iowa wheel will carry 8,000 tons and will arrive on the 13th of next month. The fourth and fifth batches have also been assigned to two ships in the United States, one loaded with 6,000 tons and one loaded with 5,800 tons. They will all set off this Saturday and are expected to arrive in Shanghai around the 10th of next month. In summary, the five batches before and after total 36,740 tons, totaling 400,000 bags. The rest of the four ships all go to the Chinese warehouses.

Shipping Goods to the United States

This time, the China Merchants Bureau directly booked the charter boats for wheat transportation from foreign shipping companies at a very low price, less than two US dollars per ton. After the first wheel, the Array Fubengk, unloads its cargo in Shanghai, it will load export goods in Shanghai and go to the United States. Its ship feet have been collected and distributed by the China Merchants Bureau and are waiting to be loaded and shipped. The China Merchants Bureau is also engaged in foreign shipping, which is the first time, and it must be recorded.

Sino-British Announcement to Be Decided This Month

As for the date of the official Sino-British telegraph announcement, according to the station, although the installed transmitter and receiver have been completed, the wiring and correction procedures are quite cumbersome. Recently, the engineer is gradually connecting the required electricity to the new machines, and testing whether there are any errors in the installed machines, and correcting the musical notes to see if they are clear. Therefore, the date of the Sino-British announcement must be determined after the new machines have been corrected. It is expected that it will be officially announced by the end of this month or early next year.

Imposing: Import Tax on Foreign Rice and Wheat

The Ministry of Finance decided to implement the collection of import tariffs on foreign rice, wheat and wheat flour on the 16th. It has been decided to collect them from the 16th of this month. The Customs Tax Department and the Customs Supervision Office have been instructed to follow the tax rate standard, which will be officially announced tomorrow (14th). As for the report of collecting anti-dumping tax, it is a rumor. The details are recorded separately as follows:

Customs Ordered to Implement

After receiving the Ministry of Finance's instructions on collecting import tariffs on foreign rice, wheat, and wheat flour on the 10th of this month, the General Customs Tax Department and the Customs Supervision Office respectively transferred the instructions to the local Jianghai Customs for reference. The tax rate method standard could have been announced earlier, but in order to prevent tax evasion and other malpractices, it was temporarily kept secret. Therefore, the outside world believes that the date of collection is set for New Year's Day next year. A reporter from the Dagon Society has inquired from reliable sources for several days and has confirmed that the import tariffs on foreign rice, wheat, etc. will be collected from the 16th of this month. The detailed tax rate method will be officially announced tomorrow (14th).

Tax Rate Standard Content

Foreign rice and foreign wheat have not been taxed in the past, but foreign wheat flour originally had a tax of 0.25 yuan per 100 pounds (that is, 2 jiao 5 fen in gold units). Therefore, the types of import tariffs collected by the Ministry of Finance this time are divided into two types: A, foreign rice is set as an increase in tax, and B, foreign wheat flour is set as an additional tax. The tax rate standard is as follows: (1) Foreign rice (old system 100 pounds equals 605 customs weights) is taxed at one yuan (calculated in gold units). (2) Foreign wheat (old system 100 pounds equals 605 customs weights) is taxed at 0.30 (that is, 3 jiao in gold units). (3) Foreign wheat flour (old system 100 pounds equals 605 customs weights) is taxed at 0.75 (that is, 7 jiao 5 fen in gold units).

Loss of Flour Merchants

The flour manufacturers in this city, such as Fufeng, Shenda, Fuxin, Shengda, and Xinda, in addition to ordering the first batch of American wheat of eight ships from the American Cotton and Wheat Affairs Office of the Central Bank, also continued to purchase foreign wheat of eleven ships directly from Chicago, Canada, Australia, Argentina, and other places. Since they learned that the tax collection period was set to be implemented on January 1 next year, the goods were all agreed to be shipped to Shanghai for delivery by the end of this year. However, after the Ministry of Finance implemented the collection of taxes on foreign rice, wheat, and wheat flour in advance, the losses were not small. According to the results of inquiries from various banks by the Dagon Society reporter, in addition to the government's own tax guarantee for the eight ships of American wheat, the direct order of the eleven ships of foreign wheat by the manufacturers will result in an import tariff loss of more than 770,000 yuan, with each ship being over 7,500 tons.

Records of Contemporary Travels

Sun Ke, Liu Weichi, Yang Dezhao, and Li Shijia took the night express train to Beijing yesterday. Yin Tong, Director of the Beining Railway Bureau, took the night express train from Beijing yesterday and arrived in Shanghai this morning.

Ministry of Communications and Ministry of Railways Detail: Method for Civil Aviation to Participate in Joint Transport: = Divided into Six Articles to Reply to the Secretariat of the Executive Yuan = = China Merchants Bureau Has Signed a Contract and Will Continue to Implement it as Scheduled =

The situation of solving the struggle of private shipping companies to participate in land-water joint transportation has been seen in previous reports. A reporter from the New Sound News Agency stationed in Beijing has obtained the original text of the official letter from the Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Railways to the Secretariat of the Executive Yuan, which has detailed regulations on the solution. The details are recorded as follows:

Repeated Requests from Private Shipping Companies to Participate

It is hereby noted that on October 5th of this year, your office's letter number 2937 stated: "By order of the President of the Executive Yuan, regarding a telegram from the Shanghai Forwarding and Customs Brokers Association stating that the Shanghai line of the joint water-land responsible transportation agreement between the Longhai Railway and the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has created a monopoly, crushing private shipping, and requesting equal treatment, etc., the Yuan has ordered the Ministries of Transportation and Railways to jointly discuss and reply. Apart from separate letters, a copy of the original telegram is enclosed for your consideration." This matter is currently under review. Furthermore, your office's letter number 3371 of November 3rd of this year stated: "By order of the President of the Executive Yuan, regarding a telegram from the Shanghai Shipping Association elaborating on the difficulties faced by the shipping industry and earnestly requesting that private shipping companies be allowed to participate in the joint water-land transportation business on an equal footing with state-run shipping companies, in order to provide relief, etc., the Yuan has ordered the Ministries of Transportation and Railways to jointly and appropriately investigate and report. Apart from separate letters, a copy of the original documents is enclosed for your consideration." This matter is also under review. Regarding the request from private shipping companies to join the joint water-land transportation scheme, the Ministry of Railways had previously responded to your office's letter number 2693, stating that "Because the joint water-land transportation is a new undertaking with many complex aspects, it is planned to extend it to private shipping companies after the railway and China Merchants Steam Navigation Company have achieved success." A letter requesting consideration was sent. Subsequently, a telegram from Chiang Kai-shek, Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission, stated that "Yu Hede and others have telegraphed requesting immediate approval for private shipping companies to participate in the joint water-land transportation scheme," requesting a swift investigation. Furthermore, the Shanghai Forwarding Association, Shipping Association, and San Bei Steam Navigation Company have successively submitted separate telegrams. After detailed deliberation, it was found that the request from private shipping companies to undertake joint water-land transportation is supported in both policy and principle.

Joint Transportation Requires Thorough Planning

However, joint water-land transportation covers a wide range and a large scale. Once joint transportation is implemented, external procedures, such as receiving and transporting goods from merchants, must be carefully protected along the way. Various preparations are necessary, which cannot be done hastily. Internal procedures, such as the railway and shipping companies allocating funds to each other, paying customs duties, transferring goods, and training employees, also require thorough planning and solid credibility to ensure smooth operation. Therefore, a joint water-land transportation contract was first signed with the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company for a one-year trial. Moreover, the railway and the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company have been discussing joint water-land transportation since the third and fourth years of the Republic of China. After years of planning, at the fifteenth National Joint Transportation Conference in the twentieth year of the Republic of China, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company sent representatives to attend and agreed on the general principles of joint transportation. By the time responsible railway freight transportation was implemented last year, the necessity of implementing responsible joint water-land freight transportation was even more keenly felt. At the sixteenth National Joint Transportation Conference this year, it was decided that joint water-land transportation was a pioneering undertaking with complex procedures, so the previous discussions were continued, and the opinions of various routes were integrated to agree on twenty-one articles of joint water-land transportation measures. Representatives of the joint transportation office, representing the state-owned railways, signed a joint transportation contract with the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to be followed. The articles of the contract either refer to the established regulations of joint water-land transportation in the East and West or are based on the established customs of various routes and shipping lines in the country, decided according to actual needs. Private shipping companies participating in joint water-land transportation must also first have a complete organization before they can be allowed. It is difficult to allow them to join without restrictions.

Six Measures for Private Participation

To uphold the established measures and the principle of equal treatment for state-run and private shipping companies, the two ministries jointly discussed and decided on six measures for private shipping companies to participate in joint water-land transportation: (1) Chinese private and state-run shipping companies may participate in joint water-land transportation, but only those that have been operating regularly on various routes since November of the twenty-second year of the Republic of China and own their own wharves and warehouses are eligible. (2) Private shipping companies intending to participate in joint water-land transportation must first submit a request to the Ministries of Transportation and Railways for approval. (3) Participating shipping companies shall establish a joint water-land transportation office, and its expenses shall be shared proportionally according to the tonnage of joint transportation cargo loaded by each company. (4) The allocation of joint transportation cargo shall be based on the proportion of ships currently operating regularly by each company, but this shall not apply if customers are unwilling to consign goods due to inadequate equipment. (5) Participating shipping companies must comply with the contract and operating rules separately established by the Joint Transportation Office of the Ministry of Railways and various railway bureaus with the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. (6) Before the establishment of the joint office of private and state-run shipping companies, the contract and operating rules separately established by the Joint Transportation Office of the Ministry of Railways and various railway bureaus with the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company shall be implemented as scheduled. With these measures, the established joint transportation contract can be implemented as scheduled, and private shipping companies can apply for participation at any time. In addition to telegraphing a response to Chairman Chiang, the Ministry of Railways will separately issue instructions to the Shanghai Forwarding Association, Shipping Association, and San Bei Steam Navigation Company. A corresponding letter is hereby sent for your review and transmission to the Executive Yuan Secretariat, Minister of Transportation Zhu Jiahua, and Minister of Railways Gu Mengyu.

Regarding the case of the Zhengzhou Yu Feng Cotton Mill Workers' Union forcibly destroying the iron gate of the factory's warehouse and taking away 369 bales of cotton yarn, the Cotton Control Association and the Chinese Cotton Mill Association had telegraphed the Central Party Headquarters for support. Please immediately order the return of all the taken cotton yarn to protect the industry, etc. This case has been telegraphed by the Central Government to the Henan Provincial Party Headquarters with instructions to promptly return the yarn." Jiaxing Sub-Customs Ordered to Close

To be converted into a wharf for passenger and cargo handling. The Jianghai Customs has received an order from the government to cease operation of the Jiaxing Sub-Customs, which belongs to the Hangzhou Customs, from January 1, 23rd year of the Republic, and to convert the site into a wharf for passenger and cargo handling. Taxation methods will remain unchanged. The original notification reads: "We have now received an order from the government instructing the Hangzhou Customs' Jiaxing Sub-Customs to cease operation on a trial basis on December 31st of this year. From January 1st of the 23rd year of the Republic, the site will be converted into a wharf for passenger and cargo handling. The taxation methods for goods transported by ships to and from the site in accordance with ordinary shipping regulations will remain unchanged. However, the taxes that were originally collected by the sub-customs will henceforth be collected by the first port customs through which the goods pass." This is hereby announced to all merchants for their information. December 11th, 22nd year of the Republic of China, Supervisor Tang Haian, Tax Commissioner Bólèdé.
