San Bei Company's Wan Xiang Vessel Causes Major Disaster Upstream of Wuxue. =A small troop transport vessel sunk in the dark of night= =More than sixty people drowned, beyond rescue=

-Over sixty people also rescued on the scene- The San Bei Company's Wan Xiang vessel, returning to Shanghai from Fuzhou, altered its route to the Yangtze River. While travelling through Yizhou, upstream of Wuxue, due to foggy conditions, the vessel struck and sank a small troop transport, resulting in the drowning of over sixty individuals. The details of this incident are recorded below.

Wan Xiang Alters Its Course to the Yangtze

The Wan Xiang vessel of the San Bei Company originally travelled between Shanghai and Fuzhou. Following the Fujian Incident, in accordance with Chairman Chiang's telegrammed instructions, the Shanghai-Fujian route was suspended and the vessel was redirected to the Yangtze River. However, the ship owners were not very familiar with the waterways of the Yangtze River, as the vessel was a sea-faring one. Therefore, the company reassigned Weng Jiqing, the ship owner of the Qingpu vessel, to the Wan Xiang, as he was more familiar with the Yangtze River route. Little did they know that a tragic accident of unprecedented proportions would occur upstream of Wuxue.

Tragedy Strikes Yesterday Morning

The Wan Xiang was carrying a large number of passengers and cargo on its upstream journey. It stopped to unload goods at Zhenjiang, Wuhu, Anqing, Jiujiang, and other locations along the way. On the 10th, after unloading passengers and cargo at Xunpu, it set sail for Hankou. At 4:20 AM yesterday (the 12th), the vessel was above Wuxue, below Yizhou. At that time, the weather was still dark, and the river was foggy. As the Wan Xiang was sailing upstream, it unexpectedly collided with a small vessel coming from the opposite direction in the dark and foggy conditions. The small vessel was broken apart and immediately sank into the river, with all those on board falling into the water.

Over Sixty Lives Lost to Drowning

Immediately after the accident, the Wan Xiang stopped, and all the crew members began rescue operations. Lifeboats were launched to search and rescue. After two or three hours, over sixty people were rescued and brought aboard the Wan Xiang. Due to the darkness, it was unknown which vessel had sunk. Later, after questioning the rescued individuals, the ship owner learned that the sunken vessel was a small military transport steaming from Hankou, carrying over one hundred armed comrades and service personnel bound for Jiujiang. Unexpectedly, the Wan Xiang struck it amidships, and the vessel sank within two or three minutes, resulting in the drowning of at least sixty people due to the lack of time for rescue.

Vessel Proceeds to Hankou After the Incident

After the tragic event, the Wan Xiang telegraphed both Shanghai and Hankou to report the accident. They also transported the rescued sixty or so people to Hankou, after providing them with clothes to change into. The Wan Xiang arrived in Hankou yesterday afternoon. The San Bei Company in Hankou has dispatched a vessel to the area around the site of the accident upstream of Yizhou to search for bodies in order to prepare coffins for burial.

Shanghai Office to Wire Report

Yesterday afternoon, the San Bei Company received a telegram from the captain of the Wan Xiang in Hankou, which stated: "The Wan Xiang vessel, at 4:20 this morning (the 12th), sank a small military transport downstream of Yizhou. The small vessel immediately sank, carrying over one hundred soldiers, etc. Sixty or so people were rescued on the scene. At 6:00 AM, we set sail for Hankou." Upon receiving this report, the Shanghai office telegraphed Hankou to investigate the truth of the incident and ordered the Hankou branch to send a vessel to salvage bodies and discuss post-incident measures.

Post-Incident Measures to be Taken

The Wan Xiang vessel sank a military transport, and many of those who died were service personnel, with the total number of drowned reaching as high as sixty or seventy people. The small vessel has been completely destroyed and submerged at the bottom of the river. It is unknown whether there will be any compensation for the victims. The matter will be determined after negotiations with the other party. As for Weng Jiqing, while serving as captain of the Qingpu vessel last month, he ran that vessel aground in Digang. The vessel has not yet been salvaged, and the company has already suffered losses exceeding ten thousand yuan. Now, he has sunk a small vessel, drowning dozens of people, which is an even greater tragedy. Therefore, the company authorities are quite dissatisfied with him. More details will be provided in subsequent reports.

British Envoy Commutes Prisoner's Sentence Before Farewell: Mrs. Hartley Spared from Death

Confined in Xiamen Road Prison. According to the "North China Daily News," the British Consulate-General in Shanghai received an unofficial notification that Mrs. Hartley, the defendant convicted of murdering her lover, Yang Ge, sentenced to death, and whose appeal had been rejected, had her death sentence commuted by Sir Miles Lampson, the British Envoy to China, on the eve of his departure for England. The official documents are expected to be delivered to the British Consulate-General this afternoon, before Sir Miles boards his ship. According to British authorities this morning (12th), the "North China Daily News" was informed that Mrs. Hartley's death sentence has now been reduced to life imprisonment with hard labor, and she will be confined in the Xiamen Road Prison in this city.

Major Fire at Long Mao Warehouse: Wool and Silk Losses in the Millions=Fireman Xiao Long Severely Injured=

The Long Cang foreign firm engages in the import and export of goods, with wool and silk being their primary items. Their warehouse is located at No. 7 Guangdong Road, comprising two buildings, one facing Edward Road and Sichuan Road, and the other facing Guangdong Road. The import and export operations of the warehouse are also located on Guangdong Road. Last year, the rear building of the warehouse was accidentally set on fire, causing extensive damage and the loss of all goods stored inside, resulting in significant losses. Unexpectedly, at approximately 10:30 PM last night, a fire suddenly broke out on the third floor of the front building. Local patrol officers noticed the fire and notified the police station, who in turn notified the fire brigade. Fire engines were dispatched to the scene, but the fire had already become uncontrollable. Simultaneously, the fire intensified, engulfing the second to fifth floors. Firemen attempted to enter the building, opening windows to allow water to be poured in. At the same time, ladders were raised to spray water from above. Tragically, a fireman named Xiao Long, badge number 301, fell from the ladder while bravely climbing it, resulting in severe injuries. He was immediately transported to the police hospital by ambulance for treatment, and his life is in critical condition. Other firemen continued to work tirelessly, but the fire was too large and flared up repeatedly. The firefighting efforts continued for a long time without much success. Around 12:00 AM, the fire finally began to weaken, preventing it from spreading further. However, the white smoke was pervasive, like a dense fog. It is feared that the fire will not be completely extinguished until this morning. As for the losses, it is said that the main items are wool and silk, amounting to millions.

Woman Uses Pig's Blood on Child's Head in Clever Money-Making Scheme

-Pretends to Give Birth by the Roadside- Yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM, behind the Yangjing Temple at the Dongyi ferry in Pudong, a middle-aged woman was sitting on the ground, with an infant wrapped in an outer garment. The infant had fresh red blood on its head, visible from the outside. The woman claimed that due to poverty, she had come out to borrow money, and while passing by this place, she had suddenly gone into labor. A large crowd gathered, and many people, thinking the woman was pitiful, offered small amounts of money to help her. At that moment, Police Sergeant Wu Ruixiang and a patrolman from the Third District passed by. Feeling sorry for the woman, Sergeant Wu ordered her to get up and gradually walk to the nearby Pudong Hospital for treatment. However, the woman initially complied, but when they reached the hospital entrance, she suddenly stopped and refused to enter. Sergeant Wu became suspicious and forcibly brought her into the hospital. After examination by the obstetrician, it was found that the woman was not in labor, and the infant was three or four months old. Thus, the scam was completely exposed. The police sergeant took her to the Third District, where the district chief interrogated her. The woman confessed that her surname was Zhu, she was 31 years old, from Taizhou, and because of poverty, she had no regular meals. She wanted to beg but was ashamed, so she had no choice but to bring out her sister's three-month-old child, put pig's blood on its head, and pretend to give birth in the hopes that others would pity her and give her money. She lived in a shack near the South Pier in Pudong. The district chief was touched by this confession. Although the woman's scheme to cheat money was illegal, it was understandable under the circumstances. Therefore, after severely reprimanding her and ordering her not to repeat the trick, he released her leniently.

Robbery and Assault in Western Shanghai: Zhang Jinfu and His Sister-in-Law Both Injured: Detectives Apprehend Three Robbers in Pursuit

Zhang Jinfu, a farmer, lives in Qiaodeng Road, Anhe Road, Western Shanghai. Yesterday afternoon around 2:00 PM, while Jinfu and his sister-in-law, Zhang Cao, were working in the fields, two men in short jackets riding bicycles approached them. Jinfu thought they were simply passersby and paid no attention. However, after reaching Zhang's house, the two men stopped, dismounted, and, leaving their bicycles by the bamboo fence, walked towards the fields. Approaching Zhang Cao, they attempted to snatch a gold ring from her hand without explanation. Zhang Cao cried out for help. In desperation, the two robbers each fired a shot at Zhang Cao, hitting her in the thigh. She fell into the field. Jinfu saw this and rushed to pursue them, reaching Fuxu Road. Jinfu happened to see a bicycle belonging to a friend parked outside. Seeing the robbers fleeing, fearing they would escape, he jumped on his friend's bicycle and gave chase. Seeing this, the robbers fired three shots at him, one hitting Zhang in the chest and exiting through his back. He also fell off the bicycle. The robbers then managed to escape. However, patrol officers from both the Public Concession and the French Concession had heard the alarm and gathered at the scene. Seeing the situation, they gave chase in all directions. Before long, they apprehended one robber in Lane 1981 on Fuxu Road and confiscated a pistol with twelve bullets. He was immediately taken to the police station. He confessed that his name was Xu Deyou and that he worked as a cook at the Tongwen Academy. At the same time, the police compared the confiscated bullets with the recovered casings. They did not match. Xu was taken to the Tongwen Academy for questioning. The academy firmly denied any involvement. The French police considered this untrue and highly suspicious. They took Xu Deyou back to the police station for further interrogation. He then confessed that he had indeed conspired to commit the robbery, but he had not fired the shots. The robbers who fired the shots were hiding somewhere on Annam Road. Upon receiving this information, the police dispatched detectives to secretly arrest them, and they apprehended two more robbers and confiscated two more pistols. They were all taken into custody at the police station, awaiting transfer to the court. Zhang Jinfu and Zhang Cao were both taken to the hospital for treatment by police vehicles. However, Zhang Jinfu's injuries were more severe, and his life is in danger.

Tragic Situation of Silk Factories' Decline

Both labor and management are in difficult situations. According to the New Sound News Agency, due to the impact of Japanese silk dumping in European and American markets, the silk market has declined. Although the government has issued public bonds for relief, it has been ineffective. Silk factories in Jiangsu and Zhejiang have almost completely closed down. Factory owners are unable to maintain operations, and instances of absconding and bankruptcy declarations are common. The situation is as follows:

Manager Flees

Of the 113 single and double-loom silk factories in this city, only 18 are barely managing to maintain operations. Each factory has suffered significant losses. The Fuxing Silk Factory on Changan Road in Zhabei, with 216 looms and approximately 300 male and female workers, has a manager who absconded due to excessive losses and owing workers over 4,000 yuan in wages. After the factory declared a shutdown on the 24th of last month, the workers still did not receive their wages. All the male and female workers were panicked and gathered at the factory owner's residence to protest. After the Fourth District Public Security Bureau sent police to persuade them, they temporarily dispersed. Yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM, all the workers once again flocked to the Sixth District Silk Industry Workers' Union in Nanlinli, demanding negotiations. Persuasion was ineffective. Fortunately, Dai Youheng from the Municipal Party Committee, Zhu Guilin from the Social Affairs Bureau, the patrol officer from the Tianbaoli Sub-Bureau of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau, and union directors explained the situation to the workers, and they dispersed. It is reported that the party and government agencies have begun mediation.

Demolition of Factory Buildings

Wu Zhu Silk Factory on Xinfeng Road, Zhabei, divided into four workshops and subleased to Fuchangtai and three other silk factories, is now experiencing a decline in the silk industry. All workshops are vacant, and a portion of the factory buildings were destroyed by Japanese bombs during the January 28th Incident. The small factory owner, Mr. Wu, decided to demolish the four workshops and convert them into residential housing. He laid off twenty-two workers who managed the machinery in the four workshops. However, disputes arose over severance pay. The Sixth District Silk Industry Workers' Union negotiated with the factory owner without success and was forced to petition the Social Affairs Bureau to handle the matter according to the law. The Social Affairs Bureau summoned both labor and management for questioning on the afternoon of the day before yesterday, but due to the intense dispute over severance pay, no resolution was reached. It is reported that the bureau decided to formally convene a mediation session.

Northeast Anti-Japanese Army General Returns to Engage in Industry =Accepts Anti-Japanese Comrades to Sustain Livelihoods= =Established Juxun Chemical Industrial Society=

Zhang Minli, the commander-in-chief of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army, invested in industry in Chengdu, Sichuan, after the failure of the anti-Japanese war. Now he has come to Shanghai to organize the Juxun Chemical Industrial Society, with Mr. Zhang serving as president. He accepts anti-Japanese comrades and promotes products, using the surplus to maintain their livelihoods. It was formally established yesterday and began operations. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 pm, he hosted a reception for local newspaper reporters on the ninth floor of the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA, reporting on the organizational process and gifting the society's products, including tooth powder and snow jade cream. He also invited the reporters to visit the society's dormitory. Details are recorded separately below.

Hosting Reporters

Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 pm, Mr. Zhang specially hosted local newspaper reporters and people from all walks of life on the ninth floor of the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA, reporting on his experience of participating in the failed anti-Japanese war and the process of organizing the Juxun Chemical Industrial Society. More than 30 newspaper reporters and guests from all walks of life attended, and each person was given a copy of the "Heartache" brand tooth powder, snow jade cream, and anti-frost honey created by Mr. Zhang.

Participating in the Anti-Japanese War

After an introduction by Yang Xinru, Mr. Zhang began his report, stating, "After graduating from the Japanese Military Academy and returning to China, I served in the military in Sichuan, as my home was in Sichuan. After the September 18th Incident, I was filled with hatred for the rampant violence of the Japanese invaders. I gathered comrades to organize a volunteer army and went north to resist Japan, engaging in the work of saving the country. Before Shenyang was lost, I discussed with Xiaobailong and worked together to attack the Huhuai Road area. With a battalion of troops, we killed thousands of Japanese invaders and seized countless machine guns and other weapons. Although our army also suffered sacrifices, our determination to resist Japan grew stronger."

Returning After Failure

"In the end, due to insufficient ammunition and lack of reinforcements, the two provinces of Northeast China fell one after another. I had no choice but to lead a portion of my comrades to retreat into the customs and seek other ways to wait for another opportunity. However, the retreating soldiers had no work to do, lacked food and clothing, and found it difficult to maintain their livelihoods. Therefore, I personally engaged in industry in Chengdu, Sichuan, manufacturing domestic cosmetics and accepting anti-Japanese comrades who had returned from the battlefield and had nothing to do as a place to settle down. To date, thousands of comrades have temporarily sustained their lives through this."

Establishing an Industrial Society

"Recently, I came to Shanghai, and many anti-Japanese comrades who had returned from the Northeast requested assistance. In order to help them support themselves and save the country, I initiated the organization of the Juxun Chemical Industrial Society, inviting them to become members. Preparations have been completed and work has begun today. All raw materials for the products come from Sichuan and are all local products. They are decorated in Shanghai, and each member is responsible for taking the prescribed items outside to promote sales every day. The surplus is enough to maintain their livelihoods. My organization of this society neither solicits donations from outside nor raises shares. I will provide guidance from time to time so that many anti-Japanese comrades can maintain their lives." Subsequently, Zhou Tiebi, commander of the Ninth Route Army and Fourth Detachment of the Northeast Volunteer Army, Huang Xuhong, chief of staff of the Iron Blood Volunteer Army, and Liu Kehen, commander of the Twenty-sixth Route Army Detachment, successively reported on the details of their anti-Japanese experiences. The speech length is omitted.

Visiting the Dormitory

The society's factory is located in the Lafayede Road Lafayede Lane in the French Concession, and a dormitory for members has been established on Lafayede Road Albert Road. Mr. Zhang hired several cars to invite reporters to visit the members' dormitory after tea and refreshments. The society's dormitory is a three-story building with a monthly rent of sixty yuan. More than twenty members live in the first, second, and third dormitories. Anti-Japanese slogans are still pasted all over the walls, but they all look haggard and quite miserable. It was not until after four o'clock that the visit ended, and the reporters were sent back. The hospitality was quite thoughtful. The society's products, under the "Heartache" trademark, first produce (1) tooth powder, (2) snow jade cream, (3) frostbite ointment, (4) talcum powder, and (5) anti-freeze honey, all of which are of good quality and low price.

Dependents of Wang Delin's Troops: Six Were Sent Back to Their Hometowns Yesterday

Those remaining in Shanghai are still being taken care of by the Northeast Refugee Association. The families of General Wang Delin's Northeast Volunteer Army have been seeking refuge in Shanghai for eight months. Daily expenses are covered by various charitable organizations, which have tasked the Northeast Refugee Joint Association with providing care. Yesterday, six people, including Liu Qinghua and Mrs. Liang Wang, requested assistance to return to their original homes in Northeast China. Representatives Zhang Chuyu and Liang Yuanshan sent a letter to the Relief Association requesting assistance. The association approved the request and provided six boat tickets and 25 yuan in travel expenses to each person. They were escorted to the Zhaonan North Station the day before yesterday to board the Puan wheel to Qingdao, and then transferred by car back to their hometowns. According to the person in charge of the association, of the three houses rented by the association at numbers 16, 18, and 25 Cai Shou Lane, Julaida Road, only the house at number 16 has been returned to the Postal Savings Bureau. Numbers 18 and 25 will continue to be rented. The report in yesterday's (the day before yesterday's) newspaper that the association had completely returned the rentals was not true. Only six people returned this time, and more than one hundred people remain here. If all the rentals were returned, the refugees would have nowhere to settle. All expenses required by the dependents will continue to be covered by the association as before.

Telegrams Sent to the Central Government and Chairman Chiang Requesting a Clear Order to Suppress the Rebellion. News from the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association

The Chinese and Foreign Relief Association on Renji Road has been receiving special representatives from various disaster areas who have personally come to the association to beg for relief. The situation is overwhelming. The disaster situation described by the representative from Gansu a few days ago was extremely serious, which has already been briefly recorded in previous reports. Now, representatives from Henan and Hebei, both Chinese and foreign, have also personally described the disaster situation in the two provinces. Details are recorded separately below. (Henan) Father Xuan Weili, a western missionary from the Street Radiant Catholic Church, came to the association specifically from the disaster area of Huaxian County. He said that when the Yellow River flooded, he personally drove a boat to rescue the disaster victims who were submerged. It is now winter, and there is still accumulated water that has not receded. Where the water has receded, the mud is very deep. If they want to restore cultivation, they do not know when they will be able to do so. Now, sorrowful cries are heard everywhere, and many are selling their children and daughters in order to survive. It is reported that in addition to the large amount of relief clothing and quilts that have already been transported to Henan Province, donations of cotton clothing and other items have been received and will be handed over to the missionary to take back and distribute first. (Hebei) Mr. Wang Fengduo, representative of the Yellow River flood, and Mr. Tian Jianai, representative of the disaster area in the three counties of Changdong and Pu in southern Hebei, arrived together. They personally described the disaster situation in Hebei, which is even more severe than in Henan and Shandong. Not only has the water not receded, but after the flood, places such as steles that were as high as ten feet were only about one foot above the silt. It is shaped like a desert, and agricultural activities have been abandoned. It is now the height of winter, how will they survive the year? The relief of the remaining people after the disaster is especially urgent. It is reported that in addition to a large number of relief clothing and quilts being transported to various disaster areas through Daokou, the association is also willing to provide assistance. However, the disaster area is too wide, and it is difficult to provide comprehensive relief. Moreover, the resources of the relief organization are limited. It is hoped that all sectors will have compassion and provide assistance.

Successful Well Drilling in Baifu and Other Three Neighborhoods

Water Problem Comes to an End

Deli Company, the landlord of Baifuli, Baluli, and Baushouli, located between Pingliang Road, Fenzhou Road, and Yangzhou Road in East Shanghai, has found that the price of tap water is too high, and the rental income is not only unprofitable, but also losing money. Although it is planned to sell or mortgage the houses in the three neighborhoods, no one is interested. Therefore, on the one hand, it refuses to pay water bills, and on the other hand, it drills wells to obtain water. Although the Shanghai Waterworks Company, a British company, has removed the water meter and cut off the water source, the artesian well drilled by Deli Company was completed yesterday. It immediately borrowed a motor to extract water for use by the tenants in each neighborhood. It is heard that the well water is still clear and usable, and the tenants are all satisfied. The water problem can be said to have come to an end, and the dispute over the landlord's inevitable rent increase can be avoided.

New Renhe Case Defendants Appeal

Chen Baosheng, the comprador of the New Renhe Steamboat in Nanshi, Shanghai, and Shen Xingsheng, the shipowner, colluded with the tea room attendants and sailors to plot the murder of Ma Kobao and four others by throwing their bodies into the river. After the case was revealed, all the witnesses were arrested and sent to the local court. After repeated hearings and clear investigations, prison sentences of varying lengths were handed down. After receiving the judgments, Chen and others still hired lawyers to file an appeal. The procuratorate of the local court dispatched police to send the entire case file and the criminals to the Jiangsu Higher Court in Suzhou for custody pending trial. It is learned that the Higher Court has scheduled a hearing for the 29th of this month in the Second Criminal Court. The Shanghai Local Court has received a subpoena from the Higher Court and has summoned the original plaintiffs and key witnesses in the case to go to the court in Suzhou on the due date to wait for questioning. In addition, the Higher Court has scheduled a hearing for another defendant on the afternoon of the 14th of this month.

Le Zhenbao Kidnapping Case: Accomplice Lu Yunlun Rescheduled for Further Questioning =Case Files Sent to the Supreme Court= =Difficulty in Conducting the Case Due to Lack of Records=

Le Zhenbao, the owner of Taichang Wood Shop on Nanjing Road, was kidnapped by bandits on the morning of December 9th last year at 9:30 am on Yuyuan Road Hed Road and held for a huge ransom. Subsequently, You A'gen, the chief detective of the Laozha Police Station, rescued Le and arrested more than ten kidnappers, including Ma Gengsheng. The First Special Court sentenced Ma Gengsheng, Guan A'fu, and Ren Xiaoxiang to death, and the rest were sentenced to varying terms of imprisonment. However, Guan and others had stated that Lu Yunlun (also known as Lu Jiting and Lu Jinbao), the owner of the Chen Linji Auto Shop on Kunming Road and a native of Taizhou, was also an accomplice. The police station repeatedly tried to arrest him but failed. Therefore, Lu's photo was printed on wanted posters. It was not until 3:00 pm on the 4th of this month that Liu Junqing, a Chinese detective from the Laozha Police Station, met Lu on Aidooar Road and arrested him. He was sent to the Special First Court for interrogation and detention. Yesterday, Judge Feng opened the court for further questioning. Zhang Shizhu, a lawyer from the police station, explained the previous situation and questioned Lu Yunlun, who denied being a bandit and claimed that Guan and others had framed him because he had refused to lend them money. He asked for justice and hired lawyer Zhan Jifeng to defend him. Judge Feng stated that the case files of Ma Gengsheng and others had been sent to the Supreme Court, making it difficult to investigate the case. It was really impossible to proceed, so he ordered a postponement for further questioning.

Tao Ergou Dies Tragically After Falling from a Building

Tao Ergou, a native of Haimen, was 26 years old and a blacksmith. He was working at the Xinrongji Construction Factory, located at No. 73 Fulili Road in the French Concession, which was contracting the construction of French barracks. He specialized in tying steel bars for cement steel skeleton projects. At around 8:00 am yesterday, Tao was working on the third floor when he wanted to bend a steel bar. Unexpectedly, the steel bar suddenly broke, causing Tao to be knocked down and fall to the ground. He broke his head, his brain matter burst out, and his flesh and blood were blurred. He died instantly. The accountant of the factory reported the incident to the French police station, which sent a detective to investigate. The body was immediately taken to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch autopsy room. The Second Special District Court was notified, and Prosecutor Wang Ren arrived at the location and determined that the deceased had indeed died from injuries sustained in the fall. The body was claimed by the deceased's uncle, Tao Sanlang, who provided a bond for the preparation of a coffin and funeral.

A Lively Play About a Female Teahouse Worker

Zhang Acai, a Shaoxing native, age 30, who works as a night-soil collector, found his wife living in house number 30, Xue Alley Bottom, North Zhangjia Alley, within the city. His wife, Zhou, is 23 years old and has a five-year-old son named Xingen. Because Zhang's monthly income is meager, he often feels financially strained at home. He asked a friend to introduce his wife, Zhou, to work as a female teahouse worker at a certain amusement park, earning a monthly wage to supplement the household income. However, after becoming a female hostess, she was influenced by the bad environment, and suddenly changed her normal behavior. She did not return home most nights and was recklessly unrestrained. Although Zhang repeatedly advised her, she ignored him. There was a rascal youth named Lu Zhaoqi, 21 years old, originally from Songjiang, who was fond of seeking pleasure with women. He usually liked to frequent brothels, chasing bees and butterflies, enjoying himself. In the summer of this year, Lu happened to visit the amusement park, met Zhou, and was amazed by her beauty, considering her a heavenly being. He often went to the park to drink tea. However, his intention was not really to drink tea. Therefore, he gave more money than others for the tea, showing off his wealth, and taking the opportunity to seduce her. Zhou also took a liking to Lu because he was young and handsome. Therefore, their hearts were in tune, and they soon had a physical relationship, using hotels as a place for secret meetings. Later, because she was madly in love, and constrained by her husband, unable to do as she pleased, she heartlessly abandoned her husband and young son in August, eloping with Lu without a trace. After Zhang discovered this, he searched everywhere for months, but still had no leads. Unexpectedly, at around 10 a.m. yesterday, he received a tip from a friend stating that Zhou was now living with Lu Zhaoqi at house number 17, Shengan Lane, Shachang Street, living together like a married couple. Zhang was furious upon hearing this and immediately rushed to the location, where he found Jiang Zhou, along with Lu Zhaoqi. He tied them both up and handed them over to Wang Baochang, the guard at the 13th post there, who took them to the third precinct of the first district. The warden, Jin, conducted a preliminary hearing. Zhang Zhou swore that she would never return to the Zhang family. Considering that the matter involved the abduction of a married woman, the warden immediately ordered the preparation of documents to be sent to the Shanghai District Court for investigation.

Record of a Quarrel Caused by a Wine Pot: Celebrating a Victory in a Lawsuit

The incident of setting off firecrackers caused more trouble. At the end of last month, Lin Chengxu and Tang Chunhua, workers at the Sanbei Shipyard on Rihui Bridge, South Shanghai, quarreled over a wine pot. Lin gathered ruffians and beat Tang Chunhua, injuring him. The police at the post took both parties to the Rihui Bridge Second District Police Station for investigation. Unexpectedly, workers from the Sanbei Shipyard gathered a crowd and rushed to the police station, attempting to seize the defendant, Lin Chengxu. After the police fought hard to resist, they scattered and fled. Later, Lin was transferred to the District Court for trial. Meanwhile, Inspector Zhang Fude of the police station reported to Li Jing, the district chief of the Second District, who was ordered to strictly apprehend the ringleader who seized Lin Chengxu and bring them to justice for verification. Unexpectedly, at noon the day before yesterday, when the Sanbei Shipyard workers were leaving work, about two hundred workers declared that they had won the lawsuit against Tang Chunhua of the Fuxingxiang Hotel and were celebrating the court's release of Lin Chengxu. The workers held firecrackers and rockets high, and set them off along Longhua Road from the factory gate, passing in front of the police station, and all the way to the south entrance of Dapu Road. They set off the rockets and threw them into the police station, causing a loud series of explosions, totaling more than thirty. When they threw them in, Police Officer Wei Zhiren happened to be standing in the reception hall and could not dodge in time, resulting in him being hit by the firecrackers and suffering unbearable pain. Furthermore, many of the workers used abusive language that was unbearable to hear. Due to the large number of people, it was not convenient to take forceful action to avoid causing trouble. However, during this time of martial law, the shipyard workers first seized the criminal and then threw firecrackers, which seriously hindered local public security. How should this be handled? It is requested to review and indicate. It is heard that after receiving the report, Police Chief Li, in addition to ordering the strict apprehension of the ringleader who seized Lin and bringing them to justice, yesterday submitted a report to the General Bureau for review and compliance.

Jin Cheng Cloth Factory on Longhua Road Robbed

The Jin Cheng Cloth Factory, located at number 491 Longhua Road, Nanshi, was robbed at 9:30 the night before last, during the night shift. Five robbers broke in, wearing gray robes or blue cloth shirts and pants. Two robbers stood guard outside the door, while three robbers broke into the inner room, displayed handguns, and forbade anyone from making a sound. They then separated and searched. As a result, they only robbed twenty yuan in cash and a gold ring before fleeing. The victim reported the incident to the Second District Headquarters of the Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Guang Ya Silk Weaving Factory on Jumen Road, Nanshi, Suffers Carelessness

The Guang Ya Silk Weaving Factory, located at number 116 Jumen Road, Nanshi, is owned by Lu Zhongying from Zhejiang. There are more than twenty workers in the factory. At 3:00 a.m. yesterday, the factory's main electrical panel suddenly caught fire, causing a conflagration. At that time, the workers woke up from their dreams, quickly put on their clothes, and immediately drew water to put out the fire. They also reported to the Fire Department, which dispatched vehicles to the scene to put out the fire. It was extinguished until 4:30 a.m., but the entire factory building had already been reduced to ashes. Afterwards, the local Public Security Bureau detained the owner's wife, Lu Yu, to inquire about the cause of the fire. It is heard that the factory had previously taken out a substantial fire insurance policy.

The Tragic Situation of the Yellow River Disaster in Hebei Province

Tian Jianai and Wang Fengduo, representatives of the Yellow River disaster in Hebei Province, reported last night at the Gospel Broadcasting Wireless Radio Station, that the Yellow River flood in the three counties of southern Hebei was so severe that they came to Shanghai to request disaster relief funds and to close breaches and repair dikes. Now, introduced by Renji Hall, they were asked to report on the Yellow River flood in Hebei Province and briefly describe the following: It has been found that this year's breaches of the Yellow River were mostly within Hebei Province. On the north bank, from Dacheji to Shitou Village, there were more than thirty breaches, flooding the entire northern bank of the county, passing through the northeastern part of Huaxian County in Henan Province, flowing into Puyang, as well as Fanxian, Puyang, Gushou, and Zhang Counties in Shandong. On the east bank, from Pangzhuang through the entire Dongming County, it flowed into Heze and other counties in Shandong. The breaches in the southeast flowed through Lanfeng, Henan, and into Kaocheng and other counties. From this, it can be seen that the water in various places was mostly from Changyuan County in Hebei Province. However, the severity of the disaster in Changyuan County broke the unprecedented record of flood disasters in the country. According to the current situation in Chang, Pu, and Dong counties, it can be divided into two points. Those that have receded have mostly become silted sandy land, more than ten feet high in some places, and several feet high in others. Those that have not receded are still in the great flood because the breach has not been closed and the major flow has not been cut off, and Puyang is still in the great flood. The former fertile fields have mostly turned into barren wasteland. It is estimated that more than 40,000 hectares of land in the three counties have been damaged, and more than 800,000 houses in villages have been washed away by the rapid currents, or silted up with sand. Even those that occasionally survived were nothing more than a tragic state of disrepair. The villages in the three counties were originally very dense, but now they have completely changed their old appearance and mostly become a desolate world. This is the first extraordinarily severe tragic situation. After this Yellow River disaster, the people of the three counties completely lost their three major elements of clothing, food, and shelter. The strong scattered in all directions, the old became starving corpses, or they sold their wives and children. It is said that a woman was sold for only seven yuan, which is heartbreaking. Some entire families were drowned in the Yellow River at that time. Therefore, there were those who committed suicide out of despair. The former wealthy households, with plenty of food and clothing, have now become destitute, without distinction between rich and poor, and everyone cannot live, cutting off this source of life. This is the second extraordinarily severe tragic situation. As for Puyang, there are still more than 680 villages in the great flood. In a blink of an eye, it is bitterly cold, the river is frozen, and the ground is covered with snow and ice. The people have neither clothing nor food to protect their lives, nor shelter to keep their bodies. How can they survive the coming years? After the disaster, many people dig for rotten grain or grass roots to take care of the present. Eating such foul things may inevitably cause epidemics to occur from time to time. According to statistics, the property losses in the three counties are more than 80 million. This is the third extraordinarily severe tragic situation. To summarize the above points, it is very different from the disaster areas in Shandong and Henan. However, Shandong and Henan are slightly farther from the breaches, so the water flow is slower and mostly silted up into fertile fields, turning misfortune into blessing, which is common. Moreover, the two provinces have a hope of a good harvest, and the collapse of houses is less, so they can avoid wind and rain, which cannot be compared with the disaster victims in the three counties of Hebei Province who have no clothes, no food, and no shelter. It can be imagined whether the disaster there is more severe than in Lu and Yu. It is hoped that the gentlemen of the country will take the purpose of disaster relief and assistance, so as to save the disaster after the catastrophe, and perhaps have the hope of revival.

Life Insurance and the Development of National Economy

— Zhang Sixu

The original purpose of life insurance is to encourage personal thrift, protect the lives of family members, and educate children. In short, life insurance is a way to consolidate personal economy, develop personal economy, and even extend to the happiness of family economic groups. From the personal point of view, investing in life insurance is nothing more than intentionally or randomly accumulating scattered sums of money gradually, until a considerable period of time, or when an agreed event occurs, to receive the predetermined whole number for use for a specific purpose. From the family point of view, most of the members of a family, except for the head of the family, are non-producers, and rely solely on the productivity of the head of the family to maintain the lives, education, and entertainment of the entire family. The life and death of the head of the family is the key to their happiness. No one in the world can guarantee the life and death of the head of the family, and their happiness is uncertainly in the hands of the god of fate, and they are powerless to resist. Only life insurance helps them to overcome the god of fate, break the mystery of uncertain life and death, and establish the triumphal arch of happiness. When the head of the family is insured for a considerable amount of life insurance, they - grandparents, parents, wife, children, etc. - do not have to worry about the future of food, clothing, housing, transportation, education, and entertainment. They are not only a blood group, but also an economically consolidated economic group. However, a blood group, lacking the chain of economic power, is easy to disperse and decline. With the addition of an economic barrier, there is no danger of collapse, so life insurance is an indispensable element of life from their standpoint.

The ultimate purpose of life insurance itself is for the family. The family is a collection of individuals, and the country is composed of families. Therefore, no matter how large or small the organization of the family is, it is the foundation of the country. The economy of the individual affects the family. The economy of the family affects the country. Although small family systems are prevalent in Europe and the United States, the lives and education of wives and children still rely on the head of the family, who is both husband and father. The organization of the Chinese state has been based on the family as a unit for thousands of years. Personal struggle and hard work are for the sake of (bringing glory to the family), and the prosperity of the family is for the benefit of (family members). Therefore, managing the family and governing the country are both the greatest responsibilities in life. Even today, although small families are advocated, the lives and education of relatives outside the small family must still be supported and maintained by those in charge of the small family. The unfortunate death of the head of a family means hunger, cold, poverty, and suffering for the entire family, which adds a burden to the national economy and a great obstacle to the development of the national economy.

Who created the orphanages and poor children's homes that we see? Isn't it a group of selfish and self-interested fathers who do not care about the happiness of their children after their death? Who are the Qingjie Halls, Old People's Halls, Relief Associations, and Vagrant Vocational Training Centers established for? Isn't it also the result of not caring about the happiness of their wives, not being willing to save money when they are young, and not providing educational funds for their children? Who raises the funds for these various charitable organizations? Is it not from local tax revenues and the burden of the masses? Local tax revenues are the government's income, which could have been used for active construction projects such as public health, education, transportation, and entertainment, but now it is better to provide passive anti-corrosion expenses. (To be continued)

An Inquiry into the Sincere Life Insurance Company's Operations

— Editor

The Sincere Life Insurance Company is an offshoot of the Sincere Department Store. To understand the Sincere Life Insurance Company's situation, one must first know the history and organization of the Sincere Department Store. The Sincere Department Store is the pioneer of domestic department stores, founded 30 years ago by overseas Chinese Mr. Ma Ying-piao and others who returned from Australia. The initial capital was only 25,000 yuan, and the scale was simple. However, with courage and determination, and an indomitable spirit, they managed and operated it, gradually increasing capital from 25,000 yuan to 200,000 yuan, then 3 million yuan, then 7 million yuan, and now it has reached a huge sum of 10 million yuan. As capital grew stronger, the spirit of the staff became more courageous and determined. Furthermore, with the revitalization of industry and the maintenance of people's livelihood and national economy as their mission, they successively established the Sincere Cosmetics Company, the Sincere Fire and Water Insurance Company, and the Sincere Life Insurance Company, together with the department store, forming the four major companies. The total capital amounts to 14.5 million yuan (with the Life Insurance Company accounting for 2 million yuan). There are tens of thousands of shareholders, all substantial Chinese merchants. Therefore, from the beginning of its establishment, the Sincere Life Insurance Company had its shareholders as its basic policyholders.

It has been ten years since the establishment of the Sincere Life Insurance Company. It has more than ten thousand policyholders, and the insured amount is approaching ten million, which is quite commendable. The difficult period for a life insurance company is usually the first decade, mainly because the initial expenses are huge, the claim rate is high, and the premiums received are few, often insufficient to cover expenses. Now that the company has safely passed its first decade and has achieved good results, it is because of its perfect organization, solid foundation, the Sincere Department Store as its backing, and the Sincere Fire and Water Insurance Company and Sincere Cosmetics Company as its left and right wings, uniting in one breath to support each other. Therefore, credit is concentrated, and all sectors enthusiastically join. The company has far-reaching expectations for its business prospects. In the future, it will undoubtedly make considerable contributions to cultivating national economic plans.

For a life insurance company to gain the trust of society, solid capital and legal operation are prerequisites. However, monitoring income and expenditure accounts to ensure accuracy is also extremely important, especially with excellent talent and scientific management.

Most of us rely on daily income to live. If something unexpected happens, our wives and children will lose their support. The only way to seek relief is through life insurance. Life insurance does not guarantee that we will live forever and never die, but it compensates for the economic losses suffered due to death. Mr. Ma Yin-chu of the Sincere Life Insurance Company, as its head office is located in Hong Kong, is registered with the Hong Kong government (and also registered with the Ministry of Industry of the National Government). The Hong Kong government has very strict supervision of accounts, and all income and expenditure figures are accurately calculated, with absolutely no perfunctory situations, which is another advantage.

Life insurance is not comparable to short-term savings. Before the age of 35, he was engaged in political life. In 1929, he was appointed as the manager of the Shanghai Sincere Life Insurance Company. During his tenure, he was able to use his knowledge and experience to make many plans, so the company's life insurance business became increasingly developed.

What is Risk?

— Gu Zhuo-lun

Explaining the definition of risk within the scope of life insurance is slightly different from the general understanding. The risk in life insurance is subject to certain conditions and has legal meanings. The conditions and meanings are explained separately below.

(1) The occurrence of the event is not predictable. Things that are foreseeable can be predicted. Having an incurable disease is a foreseeable risk. Committing suicide with a knife is also a foreseeable risk. The former is insured but not accepted, while the latter is accepted but not compensated. If, however, death occurs accidentally due to disease, capsizing of vehicles, fire and water disasters, or harm from thieves and enemies, it is an irreversible event. This is what is meant by the risk in life insurance.

(2) The occurrence of the event must be legal. What is legal? It means complying with national laws and regulations. National laws and regulations stipulate our responsibilities for our actions. If actions violate the law, the state will punish them. Killing, arson, and other illegal acts, resulting in death due to crime or death in prison, are the result of the insured's illegal behavior. The insurer is naturally not responsible. Furthermore, malicious intentions to obtain insurance money quickly and harm the life of the insured are also illegal risks.

(3) The occurrence of the event is not simultaneous. The fundamental concept of insurance is to transfer economic losses to a large number of people so that they bear the burden equally. If a large number of insured households encounter risks in the same period, such as floods or earthquakes, and the number of deaths fills the fields and cities, fulfilling the contract would not only result in claims exceeding compensation, but also in no compensation being possible. Although this type of event is not expressly stipulated by law, it contradicts the fundamental concept of insurance.

(4) The degree of risk must be estimable. Estimation means measuring the degree of risk using statistical methods. Some use age as the standard for estimation, while others use physical condition. For example, the number of deaths per year per thousand people in the 20-year-old age group, and the number of deaths per year per thousand people in the 30-year-old or 40-year-old age group can be known by referring to mortality statistics tables. This is using age to estimate the degree of risk. Another example is after a medical examination, being classified as "sub-healthy" due to physical weakness, or increasing the premium, or shortening the insurance period, with various methods. If the insured makes false statements in response to the insurance company's inquiries, or underreports their age beyond the insurance age table, or uses fraud to conceal information from the medical examiner, making the examination ineffective, the insurer has no way to estimate the degree of risk, and is not responsible if an accident occurs.

(5) The scope of insurance must be specific. If the scope of insurance is limited to limbs, the insurer's responsibility is limited to limbs. Injury to limbs is covered, but death without injury to limbs is not. If the scope of insurance is limited to accidents, the insurer's responsibility is limited to accidents. Death from illness is not covered. Therefore, the insurance contract must specify the nature and type of risk. The type is chosen by the parties involved. The insurer is not responsible if the risk is not of that type.

Enlarged Meeting of the Life Insurance Advancement Society

— Record by Fan

The China Life Insurance Advancement Society, located at 19 Avenue Edward VII in this city, held its first general meeting of company members at the Hua An Cooperative Life Insurance Company at 5:00 PM on November 23, since its recent expansion of organization. Attendees included Song Hanzhang from China Insurance Company, Xue Weifan and Fei Mengfu from American International Assurance Company, Fang Jinghe from Ning Shao Life Insurance Company, Rong Xianlin from Sihai Insurance Company, Lü Yuequan and Gu Qingyi from Hua An Cooperative Life Insurance Company, Ling Yongshu from Sincere Life Insurance Company, and Zhang Sixu from China Life Insurance Advancement Society, among others. It was a grand event. Mr. Lü Yuequan of Hua An was publicly elected as chairman, and Mr. Zhang Sixu, president of the Advancement Society, served as recorder. First, Mr. Zhang gave a brief report on the work of the China Life Insurance Advancement Society before its expansion, which can be summarized as follows: (1) Monthly publication of various promotional illustrations and texts on life insurance in famous domestic magazines such as *The Eastern Miscellany*, *Science*, *Hua Nian*, *The Woman's Messenger*, and *The Chinese Economic Journal*. (2) Timely publication of general business information and various news from various companies in local newspapers to attract public attention. (3) Monthly publication of a special issue of life insurance in the *Shen Bao* and *Shishi Xinbao*, with simple language and significant results, with publication costs shared by companies that have advertisements. (4) Collection of inscriptions and calligraphy from famous figures in the country in support of the life insurance system for viewing and promotion. (5) Dispatching members to various universities to lecture on the meaning and benefits of life insurance and to introduce aspiring young university students as recruiters for various companies. (6) Contacting the Commercial Press to publish various books on life insurance studies compiled and translated by the society (one has already been published and two are in draft form). The society's proposal was accepted by Mr. Wang Yunwu, the general editor of the press, to include life insurance topics in the newly published secondary school citizenship textbooks to explain the true meaning and benefits of life insurance. (7) The society's life insurance quarterly magazine has been published up to its third issue, with publication costs entirely covered by advertising revenue. (8) In order to promote the theory of life insurance and cultivate specialized talent, the society has started to prepare lecture notes and plans to launch a life insurance correspondence course in the shortest possible time. After the report, the meeting discussed the progress of the society's affairs. Chairman Lü Yuequan proposed various proposals from the Sincere Life Insurance Company, which were put to a vote one by one. The meeting was then adjourned. The reporter observed that the Life Insurance Advancement Society, having been established for less than a year, has already achieved remarkable results. Now, with this expanded organization, various companies can support each other to promote progress. It is foreseen that our country's life insurance industry will move forward unceasingly and be promoted and expanded. This should be taken as the starting point.

Spring and Autumn

Acting Smart

— Xin Xin

People who are truly foolish are not laughable or hateful, but those who are not smart but pretend to be, thinking they are amazing, while messing everything up, are both laughable and hateful. Because those who feel they are foolish will never be reckless or blindly rush around like a blind man riding a blind horse. They have self-awareness, realizing their abilities are inferior to others, so they are willing to work hard steadily. They are willing to humbly accept the advice of others, and they are willing to do things that others are unwilling to do. In the end, their success exceeds those who claim to be geniuses. We should not only not laugh at or hate such people, but we should also admire them and emulate them.

What about those who act smart? They only understand some superficial knowledge—no, some don't even understand the superficial knowledge, they only pick up some scraps from others—and then claim to be some kind of expert. This, of course, impresses those who don't understand this kind of knowledge, who think they are amazing. At the same time, it is not easy to expose this paper tiger's trick. As for those who understand this kind of knowledge, they find it laughable and pitiful.

What is the result for them? Because no one exposes this paper tiger—the reason being that those who don't understand are kept in the dark, and those who do understand disdain to do so—they even start to doubt themselves, thinking they have really become an expert. So they run rampant for a while, thinking they are invincible, and even start to show off in front of real experts. What happens then? They forget that their tail is not hidden—no, even if they want to hide it, they can't, because a tail is still a tail, and a fox will never become a real human. Under the microscope, their true form inevitably appears. Because they look down on everyone, and others previously found them laughable and pitiful and disdained to expose them, their behavior has now reached the point of being extremely hateful. People feel that if they are not exposed, right and wrong will be turned upside down, so they can't avoid the trouble of exposing them.

However, despite what I've said, the number of people who act smart in China is increasing day by day. The reason is that in such a chaotic year and such a chaotic society, truth is thrown into the trash can, and everything is manipulated by speculators. This kind of behavior is a shortcut to fame and fortune. Although they know that the paper tiger will eventually be exposed, by then they will have already achieved fame and profit, so they don't care.

Therefore, in China, experts in multiple fields, celebrities, and geniuses are everywhere. One person can hold ten or twenty positions or more.

Of course, they also know that working hard steadily is the right thing to do, but they feel that this is somewhat foolish and not something a smart person would do!

However, the era is moving forward, and truth will never be thrown into the trash can forever. The fox's tail may be inescapably revealed tomorrow! This, I firmly believe, and you certainly believe too.

Brief Remarks

— Zhuo

A large family is like a large ship, while a small family is like a motorboat. Only in certain environments can their characteristics be displayed.

Scolding people is a virtue, not a lack of virtue. As long as the words are just and the tone is stern, it can even be said to be "good scolding"!

In the period from a young girl to a young woman, there is a great change in style! A sharp-tongued girl often easily transforms into a gentle and amiable priestess figure. Of course, believe it or not is up to you.

Your countrymen absolutely believe in "Heavenly Father." They rely on heaven for food, they call talking "chatting with the heavens," and everything is inseparable from heaven. Therefore, everyone is indifferent to national affairs and human affairs! Because "Heaven has eyes," and heavenly justice is manifest, and retribution is inevitable. So, even if they suffer some losses, they accept it, because heaven will always provide a way out.

People say that laughing three times a day is good for the body and mind. I think crying three times a day might also be beneficial? It's a pity that neither crying nor laughing can be forced. People living in this world are truly at a loss whether to cry or laugh!

Walking

— Qian Zui-zhu

"Walking" is multifaceted and also the greatest work of mankind. If not for "unceasingly walking forward," we would not have progressed from living in caves to living in tall buildings, from eating raw meat and drinking blood to cooking delicacies, from ignorance to the era of all-powerful science.

The more civilized society becomes, the more ways there are to walk. Recently, newspapers often feature many newly invented ways of walking. Although the paths they walk are "crooked," "winding," "diverging," and "dark," it cannot be denied that they are "walking." However, their destination is either the "Huangpu River" or a "grand hotel," walking to the "death" that is the final path in life. Although "dead end" is not very pleasant, we still have to admit that they are walking hard. Because "dead end" is also a road, and a road that everyone must take, but they are just resting earlier.

Since so many people walk to their deaths, the advertising costs for these missing persons advertisements are naturally very considerable. In these times of financial hardship, a method of austerity should be considered. Therefore, I have devised a "versatile advertisement" on behalf of the advertisers. Whether it is for elopement, absconding with funds, opposition to the family, etc., it can be applied. The format is as follows:

(XX, please be advised that since your departure, the whole family is in panic ○ crying ○ weeping, ○○ is worried sick and ill, hoping you will return home immediately, ○○ can be negotiated, ○○ will not be pursued, or communicate ○○ to relieve our anxiety

XX sincerely)

Following the above format, just fill in a few words in the circled areas, and it can be applied. For example, for "seeking a runaway wife," it is very easy to create a qualified advertisement. (…children crying and women weeping…I am worried sick and ill…everything can be negotiated…the past will not be pursued…)

Attached statement: This "versatile missing persons advertisement," although invented by me, is not patented. Please feel free to use it, and there will be no lawsuits.

Dog Meat

— Nai Ling

Once the north wind blows to Guangzhou, the seasonal "masked palm civets," "dragon-tiger stew," and "five-snake feast" appear in the market. These foods, famous both at home and abroad, are local specialties. While chewing the cooked meat, except for the barking of yellow dogs being a bit unsettling, it is probably not inferior to the civet meat, cat meat, and snake meat of "masked palm civets," "dragon-tiger stew," and "five-snake feast," etc.!

What is not available in other places, we can call it a "special" food. This "special" food is regarded by the wealthy in Guangzhou as the ultimate tonic in winter. But because its price is too high, many people are unable to try it. Therefore, inexpensive and high-quality dog meat has become a popular winter tonic for the common people.

However, for some reason, the Bureau of Hygiene has designated dog meat as an unsanitary food, prohibiting its sale. Therefore, those who love it do not mind the trouble and travel long distances to villages outside the city.

In those villages, on narrow streets, there are many shops with racks full of dog meat. Inside the shops, under low ceilings, there are four or five tables no more than two feet high, and many bamboo chairs. In the center of the tables is a stove and an earthenware pot.

When we step into the shop, the first thing we smell is a rather fragrant, peculiar odor, and the second is the barking of yellow dogs waiting to be slaughtered in iron cages.

But in the end, the peculiar odor triumphs over the barking, the human heart loses its compassion, and we begin to cut the dog meat into squares and place it in a bamboo basket with a hard heart. Before the dog meat is poured into the earthenware pot, the people in the shop light a full stove of firewood, place the earthenware pot on top, and pour in prepared brown sugar, garlic, ginger, and lard to simmer. After about five minutes, the dog meat is poured from the basket into the pot. With a sizzle, the fragrance begins to spread around.

Several people surround the pot of dog meat, chatting and laughing while adding some ready-made dog broth. They put the lid on and wait for the dog meat to cook quickly. But only after about thirty minutes does the lid begin to jump. The earthenware lid is lifted, and before us is the fragrant dog meat, cooked until tender. Sipping mellow wine and chewing the cooked meat, apart from the barking of the yellow dogs being a bit unsettling, it is probably not inferior to the civet meat, cat meat, and snake meat of "masked palm civets," "dragon-tiger stew," and "five-snake feast," etc.!

The Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 20: Divination Promises Good Fortune, the Old Man Smiles Daily; Cutting Away Sorrow is Endless, Old Friends Live Across the Street

Old Zhao was perhaps more anxious about his son's marriage than his son himself. He always wanted to bring his daughter-in-law home, as it would have several advantages. First, the marriage would not change. Second, the Zhao and Yang families could cooperate in practice. Third, he could have the opportunity to hold a grandson early. However, secretly observing the attitude of the mother and daughter, they always looked worried. His son was far away in the Xifengkou defense area, and if he opened his mouth to the Jiang family, his son might not be able to return, breaking his promise and adding another layer of guilt. Conversely, writing to his son to ask him to take leave to return, if the Yang family mother and daughter were unwilling, would also make his son unable to step down. So, although he was willing in his heart, he could not express this meaning in words. He always sat in a wicker chair with old trousers for a cushion, with a dry tobacco pipe in his mouth, taking a puff and exhaling, expressing his thoughtful and awaiting response look. This time, when Jiang mentioned this issue while sitting in the chair opposite him, he clapped his hands and suddenly stood up, swinging his old voice and laughing: That would be excellent. This sentence "That would be excellent" blurted out, and the two-foot-long dry tobacco pipe also blurted out, falling to the ground with a soft thud. This dry tobacco pipe of his had a bakelite mouthpiece, and falling so violently shattered it. This old man had no companions, and the dry tobacco pipe was his only companion. Breaking the tobacco pipe mouthpiece was no different from injuring his companion. From Jiang's point of view, this was an unfortunate thing. But Old Zhao paid no attention to this, casually placing the dry tobacco pipe on the tea table, and still said to Jiang: Sister-in-law, are our intentions not the same? A parent always hopes that their son's marriage will be settled early, so they can fulfill a wish. Tell me, how do you want to handle the wedding, and I will come and record it. (266)

Short Story

Cell "Tian" Middle

— Zu Lin

Looking out through the small window embedded with iron bars, one can tell that it is already dawn. If you press your face closer to the window, you will definitely feel that the air is sharp.

Such a stimulating morning cold wind woke up two people shackled with iron in cell "Tian". They were just startled from their dreams, feeling cold and shivering. Sleep had not yet left them, and they could not help but stretch. Other than the snoring of two other people, the air in this cell was temporarily silent.

The two people's gazes suddenly met, and they gave each other a bitter sigh. Then they began their first conversation of the day.

"Damn it—not comfortable at all. A-Si brother, did you sleep well?"

"Ugh! The cold air is terrible, almost freezing me to death."

The hemp bag that served as bedding, or rather, as a coat, moved, causing another resonance of iron implements.

Yi Laowu felt a change in the contents of his crotch, as if he had an indication that he needed to urinate. He got up angrily, causing his heavy shackles to clang and clatter.

He squatted on a wooden bucket with several obvious leaks and relieved himself. At the same time, a wave of foul-smelling urine wafted up. In a cell that could only accommodate four people, in the left corner of the doorway, there was also a stinky latrine that made people want to vomit. Straw piled on the ground, with moisture constantly seeping from beneath, mixed with people's body odor, forming an indescribable smell. On the previous night, they were not accustomed to it, but once they arrived here, they had to endure it whether they liked it or not.

At this time, A-Si brother had already turned over. The other two had not yet woken up. Yi Laowu turned around, saw the light, sighed, slowly lay down, put the hemp bag on his body, and felt his head was dizzy.

The shiny silver dollars seemed to be flashing before his legs. The past could not help but reappear in his mind.

The little wild chicken's arms were as white as tender lotus roots. How could I say? This old man was ruined by those white arms! I was just enjoying myself when suddenly several soldiers came, and a child. Damn it! They said this old man was a bandit. Iron chains were put around my neck, and without explanation, they took me away. It was only a few days before they found out! Why! How did that little kid not die? He must have leaked the news.

After running for several years, I finally gained some reputation in the underworld. I even became a squad leader once and looted several guns. Over the years, I don't know how many cases we committed on the Si Hu River. We ate meat in large chunks and divided gold in large scales. We never ran into trouble. This time, something had to happen. If we hadn't drowned those sheep in the boat, such a big thing wouldn't have happened.

The next day after the crime, I heard people talking about it in the teahouse. Damn it! What Hu Fu, still a student! Ah! It's coming back to me, that young man in the blue cloth gown, wasn't he Hu Fu? At that time, this old man wouldn't have shown any mercy! I don't care if you're a student, this old man wants money. Even if you have ten wives at home, if you stir up this old man's anger, I'll still do it. Killing a few people is nothing. But this time it wasn't lucrative. There were only two hundred dollars in total. Damn it! And it made this old man suffer. What a mess! As he thought this, he felt an unnamed fire burning in his heart. At the same time, the other two had already gotten up, and the clang of their shackles was even louder than before, forming a kind of musical confession. It immediately interrupted his reminiscence, and his body began to ache.

The sunlight shone through the window, fully illuminating Yi Laowu's face. At this time, he was very reluctant to recall his past crimes. A-Si brother was busy catching lice on his short shirt. The two had been talking energetically. Before long, a soldier brought in food: a bowl of dull yellow vegetables and coarse, undercooked rice, placed on the straw. Each of them got a large bowl. Due to the pressure of hunger, they had no choice but to eat.

The heat of the sun illuminated their breakfast, as if smiling ferociously at them.

Students Who Failed the Previous Senior and Junior High School Entrance Examinations Must Register for Retake Examinations Within a Specified Time

▲ The Municipal Education Bureau Issues a Notice to All Middle Schools The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued an order to municipal and approved private middle schools yesterday stating that the students of the graduating classes of junior and senior high schools (general studies) in the current semester have been ordered by the Ministry of Education to hold entrance examinations. All students who failed one or two subjects in the senior and junior high school graduation entrance examinations in the second semester of the 21st year and need to take remedial classes may, in accordance with Article 8 of the Measures for Remedial Classes for Students Who Failed One or Two Subjects in the Graduation Entrance Examinations of Primary and Secondary Schools of this Bureau, have the remedial school submit an application to the Education Bureau to allow them to participate in the entrance examination for that subject again when the next entrance examination is held in this city, but only once. In addition, students who take remedial classes outside of school should have their original school submit an application to the Education Bureau to allow them to participate in the entrance examination for each subject again, but only once. If there are any students in the school who are taking remedial classes or taking remedial classes outside of school and should take the make-up entrance examination in this session, you are ordered to comply with the above-mentioned measures and regulations and submit a form for registration before December 20th of this year for verification. All required forms, photos, and other items should be processed in accordance with the procedures for registering entrance examination students without delay. This order.
