Weng Zhilong, President of National Tongji University, Discusses the Property Dispute of Senior Vocational Schools

The senior vocational school attached to National Tongji University in Jiangwan has been repeatedly reported in local newspapers due to a property dispute. Yesterday, Weng Zhilong, President of Tongji University, gave a speech on the history and latest situation of the matter:

The senior vocational school established by our university in Jiangwan is using part of the former Labor University's property in Jiangwan. The 354th meeting of the Central Political Council allocated it to our university for takeover. After our university received the order from the Ministry of Education and the Executive Yuan to take over, we followed the order of the Ministry of Education and established the senior vocational school. There are now more than one hundred students in the civil engineering and mechanical engineering departments. The faculty and staff hired are all specialized talents who have studied in various countries. Although it is still in its initial stage, the results are already considerable. This can be gratifying to the government and those in the community who are enthusiastic about promoting vocational education. The current plan is to add a dispensing department to cultivate dispensing talents in the pharmaceutical industry. The Labor University's school buildings were bombarded by the Japanese army during the January 28th Incident, and bricks and rubble were everywhere. They were dilapidated and had been garrisoned by the army twice. All the equipment was damaged. Our university spent tens of thousands of yuan to repair and renovate, and add equipment before it could be put in order and roughly restored to its former appearance. This is the process of our university taking over the property of the Labor University in accordance with laws and regulations and establishing the senior vocational school. However, the Labor University's school buildings were mortgaged to the Shanghai China General Chamber of Commerce Bank during the era of the former vagrant model factories. After the Labor University opened, the China General Chamber of Commerce Bank repeatedly negotiated with the Labor University, but to no avail. Therefore, it filed a lawsuit with the court. After the Labor University was closed, the Ministry of Education organized a management committee to manage the former Labor University's property. The bank continued to file lawsuits, and recently the court ruled that the property would be seized. The university believes that the occurrence of this incident will have a great impact on the foundation of the attached senior vocational school. The author has repeatedly gone to Beijing to present the matter to the Ministry of Education and ask for instructions on how to handle it in order to maintain the production education that is urgently needed in our country. I also asked Mr. Song Wusheng to conduct reconciliation, but the bank's conditions were harsh and difficult to accept in fact. We also invited the bank to hold direct negotiations between the two parties so that their opinions could be reconciled. However, the bank refused and insisted on being a creditor. In fact, from the perspective of Tongji University, the takeover of part of the Labor University's property and the use of the Labor University's school buildings were completely done in accordance with orders. The property of the former vagrant model factories was established by the Shanghai Political Branch in accordance with the measures for handling public property when the revolutionary army arrived in Shanghai during the Northern Expedition. The transfer of property has been transferred many times to this day. Our university is not the subject of the debt. This is clear. Moreover, this debt has long been handed over by the central government to the Ministry of Finance's Committee for the Reorganization of Domestic and Foreign Debt for overall handling. The transfer of debt is a uniform measure by the Ministry of Finance to handle the correct or potentially considered various debts of public and private institutions of the government before the revolution. This disposition measure has special characteristics and is very different from the transfer of general debt. If ordinary legal sanctions are used, there are many practical obstacles. Therefore, this debt has nothing to do with our university. The reason why our university is trying to compromise and negotiate with the bank is to take into account the importance of production education and to prevent the vocational school, which has already been on the right track in a very short period of time, from being unable to settle down, which would affect the progress of their studies. The bank has insisted repeatedly, which is regrettable. Furthermore, the land mortgaged to the bank has buildings such as office buildings, gymnasiums, dormitories, and bell towers built on the part used by our university during the Labor University era. After our university took over, it was greatly repaired, and the factory machines were repaired and reorganized, which cost a lot. The increased value on the ground and the repair and addition of machinery cannot be completed by mere seizure. The bank, as a financial institution, should uphold the government's intention to support production undertakings and revitalize production education as its responsibility, and should not treat it as a normal debt-debt handling method in commerce, which would cause other misunderstandings. Currently, the faculty and students of the affiliated vocational school are indignant at the righteous debt and have spontaneously organized a school protection association to resolutely oppose it. The crowd is angry, and the sounds of study will fall into stagnation. The author is eager for this unfortunate incident to be resolved as soon as possible so that it will not expand further. At the same time, I deeply hope that the national education community and people in society who promote vocational education will give it sympathetic assistance and visit and provide guidance at any time so that society can learn the truth after the establishment of our university. I would be very grateful.

Free Talk

Distinguishing Critics

— Lushuang

Nowadays, when one mentions "critic," people imagine a cold and stern face—furrowed eyebrows, (piercing) eyes, an unforgiving mouth; moreover, (wielding a pen like a mighty beam), finding fault with everything, this isn't good, that isn't right, a third thing is insufficient; in short, more criticism than praise.

This is naturally a (fantasy). Critics aren't people whose brains are structured differently, who specialize in (picking bones from tofu), who necessarily turn good things into bad; a critic is merely (in their professional capacity), unable to compromise and follow the crowd. A truly responsible critic, if forced to criticize more than praise, must feel a pang of sorrow, for his joy lies in discovering and reading great works, and recommending them, certainly not in tearing everything down.

There are also (critics) in the world who can't see anything good; they scold (the petty bourgeoisie) for being too vulgar, and they're also dissatisfied with people who relentlessly pursue an ideal, deeming them too idealistic. Such critics are so-called (nihilistic) critics. There have been many such critics in the history of Western literature, but they can't truly (be nihilistic), tearing down everything; they still praise nihilistic works.

I recall a story about a play on stage portraying Cao Cao. A woodcutter, upon seeing Cao Cao appear, was overcome with rage, jumped onto the stage, and killed him with an axe. There's a similar story from the Middle Ages in the West: the killer was a peasant, and the victim played Judas, who betrayed Jesus. Though Cao Cao and Judas are killable, the woodcutter or peasant mistakenly thought the author was advocating for the characters' actions, assuming the thoughts of the characters in the book were the author's thoughts, and thus the (punishment of the axe) was almost directed at the author.

In a chaotic society, the former type of critic often gains the title of most (thorough), while the latter type often gains the title of most (courageous). With many (thorough) and (courageous) individuals, critics are thus generally misunderstood as cold, frightening, and solely focused on nitpicking (fault-finding), which isn't accidental!

A Record of Peril at Xianxia

— Yu Dafu

Journeying south from Quzhou, one is constantly greeted by verdant mountains, surpassing even the azure rivers in hue. Traversing a vast plain, passing the Twin Pagoda, one arrives at a walled city ensconced by four mountains – Jiangshan County.

Jiangshan is renowned for its Jianglang Mountain with its three towering rocks. Crossing Xianxia Pass southwards leads directly to Fujian and Guangdong; heading west to Yushan reaches Jiangxi. Being a nexus of seven provinces, Jiangshan is indeed a crucial border post. In these times of turmoil and famine, the apprehension and timidity of the people of Jiangshan County can be readily imagined. Our journey southward is merely to witness the perilousness of Xianxia Pass; indulging in local customs, leisurely strolls amidst nature, and water-side excursions are luxuries ill-afforded this year. Thus, on the second day in Jiangshan, we hastily chartered a car to Xianxia Pass.

Boarding the car outside the South Gate station, three li brought us to Jingxing Mountain, locally known as Dongyue Mountain, beneath which lies Tiger Rock and a pagoda erected during the Ming dynasty's Jiajing era. Twenty li southwards, the soaring Jianglang Mountain, with its three colossal rocks, vaguely comes into view, now coalescing, now separating, leaping amongst the eastern mountains. Further along are Yutou, Gorge Mouth, and the Xianxia Ridge area. Despite the journey to Jiangshan being eighty or ninety li, the car traversed it in merely two or three hours.

The countenance of Xianxia Ridge is truly magnificent – from afar, one perceives the vast Xianxia mountain range stretching for a hundred li; closer inspection reveals an impenetrable veil of sky. On the east, west, and south sides, valleys within valleys, mountains upon mountains abound: countless peculiar peaks, strange rocks, ancient trees, and lengthy vines. Most tortuous and confusing, defying all sense of direction, is the newly constructed highway from Guanwai's Twenty-Eighth Township, tracing the Dragon Creek and Transforming Dragon Creek, two major rivers in the deep mountains, leading to Jiangshan.

Every five steps a turn, every three steps a climb; on one side a swirling abyss of ten thousand fathoms, on the other a precipice of a thousand layers unreachable by birds. Each turn unveils a new vista, each climb reveals a new realm. Ascending and descending, going to and fro, we journeyed through the Xianxia mountains, along the Dragon Creek banks, heading south from the north, circumnavigating Xianxia Pass; the car traversed the mountain road for a full hour. The mountain's height, the water's depth, the plethora of turns, the road's peril – described unreservedly, it surpasses Hangzhou's Nine Creeks and Eighteen Ravines by at least three hundredfold. To witness the winding mountains and waters, to test the road's ruggedness, to gamble with life and fortune, to taste the extraordinary thrill of a life-or-death adventure, Xianxia Ridge is a must-visit, especially the newly constructed highway that circles from Xianxia Pass's northern foothills, exiting the pass and ascending to the Twenty-Eighth Township south of the pass. As the car reached Pidan, passing the narrow pass of Xiaowu Ridge, peering down at the residences at the bottom of the Twenty-Eighth Township Valley, and gazing at the azure shadows of Pucheng's Maple Ridge peaks in the distance, I truly experienced an indescribable sentiment – a mixture of joy and fear. Joy at having traversed many perilous passes beyond the pass, and fear at the direct view of the destination, the Twenty-Eighth Township at the foot of the mountain, though separated by merely the space of a catapult shot, the mountain slope is steep and sheer, plummeting down some two or three thousand feet. Turning back to look at Xianxia Pass at this moment, a former bird path paved with stone steps resembling a snake's belly is already hidden high amidst the clouds and trees.

Descending from Xiaowu Ridge's narrow pass, circling and winding for another thirty or forty minutes, arriving at the Twenty-Eighth Township outside Xianxia Pass, a wave of goosebumps suddenly erupted upon everyone's skin.

The sun was clearly shining brightly, the sky was naturally azure, and the tall residences were arranged layer upon layer, but the people – the living, breathing people – where had they all gone?

Many neat residences had windows shut, but doors ajar, half-open, or even yawning open, resembling the mouths of dead bass. Stepping inside revealed only scattered straw on the ground. The echo of footsteps reverberating in the empty house filled one with fear. Suddenly, a rustling in the dark corner of the room, amidst the straw, would occasionally rouse a person, but with only bare eyes, they would size you up and silently evade. If you pursued them with a question, they would reluctantly stop, give you another bare-eyed assessment, shake their head, reveal a ghastly smile, and then depart, uttering not a single word. (To be continued)

Rural Scenery

— He Deming

Little Scabby was dazed on the straw pile. The sun was setting in the western hills, and the cows were mooing, but he paid no attention. Only those dark eyes, like two stars, kept flashing before him.

(Ah Qiao, that little girl! She's got some flavour.)

He blurted this out involuntarily, his mind clearing. Seeing that the sky was getting dark, he quickly stood up, took his sickle, and led the cow home. Just as he approached the fence, he ran into Ah Qiao.

(Little Scabby, you're back! Why so late?)

She said, laughing all the while.

(Sister Ah Qiao, …)

Little Scabby couldn't find the words, just staring at her.

(Hurry inside, don't let Brother Ah Niu see you again, or you'll get a slap.)

She still kept laughing. As soon as Little Scabby heard her mention her fiancé, Brother Ah Niu, he became unhappy. He glared at Ah Qiao fiercely and went inside.

In the evening, Ah Qiao was cooking in the kitchen. Little Scabby was enthusiastically throwing bundles of bean husks into the stove, feeling an indescribable comfort in his heart. His eyes, like a hungry wolf, kept darting towards Ah Qiao's face, her body, … from top to bottom, from right to left, circling, circling.

(You rascal! Why are you staring at me? I don't have flowers growing on me.)

Ah Qiao raised the tongs, feigning anger, wanting to hit Little Scabby.

(If you don't look at me, how would I know I'm looking at you?)

Little Scabby said, grinning slyly, while picking up a pine cone from the woodpile and throwing it, hitting her cheek.

(Ouch… Damn it!)

She touched her face, blushing.

(Ha… ha… hee… hee…)

Little Scabby laughed until he couldn't breathe. Just as they were laughing, Brother Ah Niu suddenly ran in.

(What are you laughing about again? Hurry up and take the dishes out!)

He looked at Little Scabby under the stove and said:

(Always making a racket, I'll feed you willow branches!)

Little Scabby pouted, ignoring him.

He left. The kitchen was silent, with only the sound of boiling oil and the crackling of bean husks.

Notes from a Guest's Window

— Shu

Fifteen

Many articles from the past, if well-edited, often become more excellent than the original. Especially with descriptive articles, removing those pedantic arguments and vulgar beginnings and endings, they can almost become masterpieces. I personally enjoy doing this very much. For example, Wang Heng's "Record of Watching Peach Blossoms at the East Gate," I once removed the beginning and ending of the full text, making it into the following short piece:

My nature is uniquely fond of peach blossoms, and I never fail to visit them every spring, and I always go to remote places. On the seventeenth day of the second month this year, I made an appointment with Ru Zeng, sending someone to explore the four corners of the city, asking where the flowers were blooming and going there. They reported that the East Gate was good, so I walked out of the East Gate, stepping through rapeseed flowers, and saw a village residence with some willows and peach trees to admire, so the wine jars and mats were set up in order. The residence was in a small stream, with peach blossoms on either side. There were about thirty or forty trees on the stream, very tender and beautiful. Then we moved to the Wu family's estate, where the estate and pond were intertwined. It was similar to before, but five times as large. The flowers were large and abundant, with a scarlet color in the middle, especially the ones by the water. Several tall poplars stood outside the pond, like great men in official attire, guarding young women inside. The peach blossoms were also drunk, drooping their faces, washing their makeup by the water, not easily showing their foreheads. We drank under the trees for a long time.

This can be said to be a wonderfully concise descriptive piece. However, the original text was as long as 505 characters, with the opening taking up 35 characters and the later vulgar and pedantic arguments taking up 289 characters. Removing 324 characters, leaving 181 characters, makes it into this article. For many works from the past, I think those studying ancient books can put in some effort to organize them in this way. But my intention is not to have everyone be fascinated by ancient bones. Fascination with ancient bones is very different from the study of ancient books.

The Two Brothers (57)

— Translated by Li Weike, Written by Maupassant

Since receiving the inheritance, Zheran had been considering every day whether or not to marry her. Every time he saw her, he felt he had decided to take her as his wife, but then, when he was left alone, he thought he might as well take his time to consider it again. Now she was not as wealthy as him, because she only had an income of about twelve thousand francs a year, but her wealth was all real estate, land in the Le Havre basin; and such real estate would be worth a great deal of money in the future. In this light, their assets were about the same, and he really liked the young widow.

This day, watching her walk ahead, he thought to himself: (Okay, I have to decide. I certainly won't find anyone better than her.)

They advanced along a sloping valley that descended from the village to the cliff: the peak of the cliff overlooked the sea at the end of this valley at a height of eighty meters. In the frame of the green coast that sloped down to the left and right, a triangular piece of water, as blue as silver in the sun, appeared in the distance, and a sailboat that was almost invisible floated there like an insect. The sky and the sea, full of sunlight, were not mixed together, and it was simply impossible to distinguish their boundaries: the two women who walked in front of the three men drew their figures wrapped in short clothes on this bright horizon.

Zheran's eyes were bright, watching Mrs. Lumei's slender ankles, delicate legs, graceful waist, dazzling large straw hat, etc., flee in front of him. This kind of escape further aroused his desire, gradually adopting the kind of determination that hesitant and cowardly people suddenly adopt. And the warm air mixed with the scent of the coast, Ajone, alfalfa and grass, and the fishy smell of the rocks exposed on the water, slowly intoxicated him on the one hand, and made him more excited on the other hand. With every step he took, every second he passed, and every time he looked at the lively figure of the young woman, he became more and more determined: he decided not to hesitate any longer, and decided to tell her that he loved her and wanted to marry her. Shrimp hunting could be used by him, making it easy for them to have a chance to whisper; and this was also a beautiful environment, a beautiful place to talk about love, inserting their feet into the depression filled with clear water, and watching the long whiskers of the sea shrimp escape under the seaweed.

When they reached the end of the valley, to the edge of the abyss, they saw a narrow goat path descending along the cliff. At their feet, between the sea and the foothills, near the mountainside on the left, was a pile of amazing boulders, collapsed, collapsed, and piled in a mess on a undulating plain covered with grass, which ran south until it disappeared. This plain, which was caused by the collapse of the coast in the past, was covered with thorns and swaying shallow grass. The rocks that fell from the volcanic eruption looked like the ruins of a large city of endless white walls that had disappeared from the coast and overlooked the ocean.

(Ah, this is so beautiful,) Mrs. Lu stopped and said.

Zheran caught up with her, his heart pounding, and reached out to help her down the narrow stairs carved into the rock.

They walked in front, while Captain Boqiru fixed his body on those two short legs, stretched out his bent arm to Mrs. Roland, who was dizzy with the abyss.

Roland and Bill went down last. The doctor had to lead his father, Roland, who was simply so dizzy that he had to let his son drag him down one step at a time.

Securities: Major Players Accumulate, Public Bonds Rise

▲ Possible Short Squeeze in This Month's Contracts

Yesterday, the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange saw a reverse trend from the previous day, with prices rising steadily. Major players were actively buying, and swap transactions were also lively. The trend indicates a possible continuation of the price increase. The financial sector is under strict scrutiny by the Ministry of Finance, and due to year-end accounting, funds are being held rather than released. In terms of the political situation, the Guangdong faction is gradually moving closer to the central government, and the Fujian situation lacks the potential for external development due to various factors. Rumors about political instability are unfounded. In terms of trading volume, there are currently several accounts with a combined balance of 3.3 million taels for this month. It is reported that several firms, including a certain company, plan to acquire approximately 1.5 million taels. One or two major sellers, who delivered spot goods last month in significant amounts, are unlikely to deliver all goods this month. Therefore, a short squeeze is still possible. The overall situation is expected to become clearer soon, especially as the delivery date for this month's futures approaches. The volatility is expected to increase further, so we should wait and see. Yesterday morning's two trading sessions saw prices start small and then rise, followed by prices starting high and then falling in the second session, still in a chaotic and fluctuating state. Flour and Wheat Prices Rise Together, Grain Prices Increase

Tax on foreign wheat will be implemented

Flour Market: After the market opened in the morning, the prices for various months saw a jump, with the price of foreign wheat generally improving by about one jiao. The anticipation of increased taxes also fueled activity, causing market sentiment to be exceptionally bullish. The opening prices for the current month and distant months increased by about three fen compared to the previous day. Trading was particularly active at that time. However, in the second session, manufacturers took advantage of the situation to actively sell off their stocks, causing market sentiment to soften by 0.01 yuan. When the market opened in the afternoon, the current month's contract briefly broke through the 0.03 yuan mark due to some buying from customer guilds. Market rumors that the tax on foreign wheat would be implemented, with an actual increase of 0.54 yuan per dan, and the rise in futures prices greatly impacted market sentiment. However, major manufacturers continued to release stocks, causing the situation to ease again. As a result, the current month's contract rose by 0.0325 yuan compared to the previous day, the January-February contract rose by 0.0225 yuan, the March-April contract rose by 0.025 yuan, and the May contract rose by 0.0275 yuan.

Wheat Market: After the market opened in the morning and afternoon, the prices for various months saw a uniform surge. In the morning sessions, the price of foreign wheat improved by another jiao, and because there were few sellers, bullish sentiment was exceptionally strong. Therefore, opening prices for all months, especially distant months, improved by 0.03 to 0.05 yuan. When the market opened in the afternoon, it was rumored that the tax on foreign wheat would be implemented and announced soon, with a tax rate of 0.54 yuan. As a result, market sentiment inside and outside the industry turned more expensive, and there was active buying of distant months' contracts. Because there was no limit on purchase prices, the market expanded step by step. This situation was indeed driven by the increased tax. As a result, the current month's contract rose by 0.04 yuan, the January-February contract rose by 0.1 yuan, the March contract rose by 0.12 yuan, and the April contract rose by a significant 0.15 yuan. Spot wheat trading was very quiet, with only 250 bags of Bengbu wheat opened throughout the city at a price of 4.25 yuan.

Promote Childbirth - New

Recently, I saw such a piece of news in the newspapers; (Reuters Berlin: The Hitler government recently issued an order to encourage young men and women to marry, stipulating that married men and women can borrow money from the government to purchase furniture and other items. The plan has now taken effect, and 10,000 people in Berlin have applied to the registry for loans, 5,000 of whom have been approved, 847 have been rejected, and the rest are still under consideration. Unmarried couples can receive up to 600 marks) This shows Germany's attention to the country's population.

There are three types of oppression that our country has suffered from the great powers: political oppression, economic oppression, and population oppression. In recent years, our country has often been oppressed by the great powers, coupled with domestic and foreign troubles, natural disasters, and man-made disasters. The only thing we rely on is that our country has a population of 400 million. When we fight hand-to-hand with foreign countries, we can resist ten to one. However, the number of people lost due to war and natural disasters is also a huge number! Looking back at the increase in the population of the great powers, it is unexpectedly rapid, but what about us? There is a decrease but no increase. After all, we will complete the three major oppressions of the great powers.

Yesterday, I watched the Soviet sex education film (Healthy Women), which is far better than the delicate, erotic, and fleshy film that can only anesthetize people. I know that the physiological changes of women do not need to be kept secret, but need to be studied and guided openly. (A healthy nation is produced by a healthy mother, so if you want to strengthen the race, you must first strengthen the mother's body) This is what this film tells us with pictures and subtitles.

Let's take another look at our quaint motherland! Widows should observe chastity, and nuns should be lonely for life; otherwise, they indulge in licentiousness and absurdity, spreading the seeds of weak races and extinct nations.

A Young Girl's Mood - Wen Bing

The garden is gradually becoming somewhat different from before. From her letters, it can be clearly seen that a young girl's mood is soaring upwards. Before, she didn't write often, and would only send me a simple report when there was something to say. Her words were so solemn, she didn't easily reveal a line of her mood, she didn't easily say a slightly provocative love word, she was so poised and demure, and she treated me with such respect and courtesy that I almost suspected she was a (stone woman). As for me, because I was older than her, my knowledge was naturally higher, and I knew that a young child like that must not be disturbed by my own mood, or by some attitude, so I always put on a teacher-like face, and always told her big words. For example, she asked me about the mood of spring, why it was always flustered and strangely melancholic, and I told her that it was entirely the influence of nature, the reason for the (moving) spring phenomenon; she asked me how she could learn to write articles, and I told her to read more, read more, do more, and think about actual life more often; she told me that her body was very weak and often sick, and I told her to exercise more.

We just went back and forth like this, although we have known each other for more than a year, but in fact, in reality, it is like a superficial friendship. This, I still think is good at the moment, because our circles of life are so narrow, I have unspeakable bitterness, and she is being bound by her family, unable to get the understanding of her brothers, and living in tension and anxiety every day. In this way, if we simply (you come and I go) talk on paper, it will undoubtedly exacerbate each other's troubles, and even bring out some inexplicable pain. I just want to struggle desperately to see how I can get a small paragraph of my own after three or two years. If I am struggling to live at that time, we can share the joys and sorrows and live together. All the previous wounds will be washed away at that time. I have subtly hinted to her about this meaning several times, and she probably understands it, so she often encourages me and my dreams, hoping that some branches can blossom and bear fruit.

However, she has gradually become somewhat different lately. Not long ago, she sent a letter, like an aggrieved letter, full of suspicion and even a hint of blame. It was three pages long, but the meaning was very simple, that is, I should not always put on a teacher-like posture to her. She can be a teacher-like wife, but she cannot really be a teacher's student. She also cited many examples, such as how so-and-so's fiancé addresses so-and-so in his letters, and what kind of words are in the letters. After reading them, her constricted heart seemed to have been nourished. If I had such a letter to give her, how happy she would be!

There are also some letters that mostly say that because she misses me so much, she even spaces out when reading a book or attending class, and often can't sleep at night, and often feels flustered for no reason, wondering if I am like this too. She longs for me to tell her these things without any concealment.

Sometimes I write to tell her that I am sick, and she sends letters one after another, saying that she has unspeakable pain and guilt, because she cannot serve and comfort me, and the letter cannot convey her mood.

Also, she said that her mother is unwilling to bear her tuition fees, and her brothers and sisters-in-law are laughing at her, which makes her unbearable.

Of course, these cannot be said to be completely untrue.

However, I am thinking more: her young girl's mood is soaring upwards, and she not only eagerly needs tenderness in correspondence, but also needs (more than this) sustenance.

Made on December 6, 22.

Seeking the People - Qu Chen

One evening, after finishing dinner, I sat alone in my study, about to spread out paper and grip my pen, focusing my mind in deep thought, when suddenly it seemed I saw something. It was as if I were standing on a main thoroughfare, looking around blankly, not knowing where to go. Suddenly, I saw a person coming from the east, wearing leather shoes, carrying an umbrella on their shoulder, and walking hurriedly. I stepped forward to ask, "Sir, where are you going in such a hurry?" The person did not have time to answer, and kept wiping the sweat from their forehead. After waiting for them to catch their breath a little, they said, "I am a giant speculative merchant, a skilled salesman, and my livelihood depends entirely on running around. I am also good at using my tongue to persuade people, and some people call me a running dog. Now, because public bonds have stopped trading and gold prices have fallen, my business has suffered, and I am feeling depressed. Recently, I heard that the price of (the people) has soared, and there is a lot of profit to be made in this. However, this item is not entered much, and I am going around looking for it, not hesitating to rush about. If you can accompany me, you will have a lifetime of endless eating, wouldn't that be better than staying at your desk all day for a few yuan of manuscript fees?" I was bored, so I replied, "Okay!"

So, we went west together. On the way, we passed Yangshu Pu and arrived at Caojia Ferry. There was a worker sitting with his machine stopped. We went forward and asked, "What is your esteemed surname, worker?" He replied, "My surname is Min." The man was overjoyed, his face beaming with a smile. He patted the worker on the shoulder and said, "Happiness has come! Why suffer like this! Today, the world is ruled with morality, and common people are valued. The government is newly established, called (the people), production belongs to the public, and labor is supported. If you can follow me, you will have endless happiness!" The worker laughed and said, "Sir, you are thinking too much! Aren't you at the end of your rope? I have two hands, as strong as iron, and I have two feet, as fast as the wind. Happiness is sought by oneself, why wait for it to be given to me, relying on others will end in disaster! Please look at the public figures who are in power now, which one of them is not rich? Which one of them is not sitting high and mighty, and whose sedan chair is not carried by us, the people? But in the political arena, everything depends on deception. Once they ascend the throne, they will kick the sedan chair carriers into the west wind. Empty promises have already filled boxes and cages. Today's failures are none other than yesterday's heroes, what difference is there between them, and what west or east is there! There are only a few tricks, and I dare not go along with them again! Sir, please be wise and turn your sails quickly!" After speaking, he did not answer. The man was dejected, and tugged at my clothes to go further. In a daze, I couldn't tell west from east. I vaguely saw a person lying in the field. I went closer to see, it was an old man. The man was delighted and said, "The consciousness of the worker is ultimately not new, now looking at this old man, he has a lot of spirit, the true people, are they not here?" So he shook him to wake him up. The old man woke up with a start, rubbed his old, blurred eyes, and pointed at the two of us, saying, "Who are you gentlemen? Why have you come to see me?" The man replied, "Old man, what are you waiting for here? The dew and wind are blowing, won't you be harmed! Tilling the fields for others, the worthy men of the past did not do, the new policy of today, the ancient customs can be followed, allocate fields by population, won't that come about!" The old man heard these words, and suddenly became furious. Pointing his finger like a halberd, he said, "You brokers, only know how to make money, running around, and telling lies over and over again. In the revolution the year before last, I lost two sons, and I have a grandson left to sleep with me, old man. The exactions have not been removed, and miscellaneous taxes are continuous! Working hard all year round, I don't have enough food or clothing, crying for hunger and cold, who pities me, who pities me? The rich people and old people, all don't ask. I'm just prolonging my life, waiting for the end of my life. Now that there is a shortage of sedan chair carriers, you are coming again, look at the past mistakes, what else is there to say!" The man traveling with me heard this and quickly said, "No, old man is old, and afraid of war, but please go to the west of the city, and act as an old-fashioned person, no other procedures are required, just shout the slogan three times, not (going through fire and water), but just expressing a little public opinion! When the great project is completed in the future, everyone will have glory, not only will I feel grateful, but also share the peace." The old man said, "You do your dreams, I have awakened from my dream, how many white bones have created how many famous names, ordinary monsters and demons, can't do fresh things, if you want to enjoy peace, you should still manage it yourself. I will see where the hoe rises, and hear the sound like thunder. Please don't disturb my sweet dream, I will wait for dawn." The old man finished speaking, and immediately fell asleep on the field, snoring. Pushing him, he would not wake up, calling him, he would not respond, interviewing twice, I couldn't find a true person. The man's face was dejected, and he seemed to have lost something. Staggering forward, I suddenly saw a broken pear tree by the roadside, and took his two Buddha statues to leave, saying that it was just to fulfill his responsibilities, and it could also be used for emergencies. When shaking hands to say goodbye, I suddenly woke up, and my body was still one step out of the study.

The exchange market opened with recent selling prices of British exchange at one shilling three and a half pence and US exchange at $33.125. Zhaofeng, Changda, Xingyong, Yuanmao, Yong, and others advanced, rising from $3.1 to $4.7. Meifeng, Zhengjin, and Cyprus March US dollars at $34, Yuanfeng, Yongzhi, Fengyong, Bingxing, Hengxing, and others divested, retreating to $2.5. It was anticipated that HSBC would quote British rates at par and American rates down by half a yuan. Yida, Yongchun, Yuanyong, and others advanced forward contracts. Mitsui bought April US dollars at 3.125, rising to $4. Due to Overseas Chinese and Huabi selling March US dollars at 0.0625, Fuyu, Zhengchang, Hengxing, Zhifeng, and Yong sold down to $2.2. Mitsui bought March US dollars at 1.125, pulling up by one yuan. Hengtai made some purchases. Then, Zhengjin and Overseas Chinese sold March US dollars at 1.125. Hengxing sold forward contracts repeatedly, and the rate retreated to $1.3. Hongli and Yuanmao Yong advanced forward contracts, with the situation remaining relatively stable. Zhaofeng Chang also bought back to over $2. Mitsui took in April US dollars at 3.375, and Huixiang advanced forward contracts, returning to a rise. The noon close was $712.5, with merchandise auctioned at $2.2.

The afternoon market opened at $712.4, with merchandise opening at $2.4. The market opening was flat. Sumitomo sold, while Shanghai bought April US dollars at 3.375. The situation was quite stable, hovering around $2.5. Then, Shanghai sold February US dollars at 8.125. Wanxing and Yuanshengyong divested, retreating to $1.7. Zhaofeng Chang, Zhifeng Yong, Qianchang and Xianglian jointly bought forward contracts. Banks traded April US dollars at 3.7, gradually rising to $3. Yuanmao Yong also advanced. Hengyu divested, but Ruixing replenished, and although there was a setback, there was much fluctuation. Gradually, Zhengjin and McCallie sold March US dollars at 0.0625, falling to $2.1. Later, trading was not active, lacking change, and hovering uncertainly. Although merchandise was sold, Yuanheng and Shunli slightly took in. The close was $712.3, with merchandise auctioned at $2. After the close, Daxing Yong, Shunmao, Yuanmao Yong, and Dadecheng made some supply, falling back to within $1. The situation reversed to fatigue. The highest price of the day was $714.7, and the lowest price was $711.3, a difference of only $3.4. As a result, it recovered $10.05 from the previous close.

The posted price was reduced by half a yuan by HSBC, to $32.875. The standard gold price was $730, approximately $18 more than the closing price. Therefore, the previous close was about half a yuan lower. The ledger price for this month was $719, January was $713, the morning call money rate was $719, and the afternoon call money rate was $718. The "烚赤" price was $1,079, with the situation uncertain. London spot gold rose six pence from yesterday, which made the market conditions slightly stable. Trading in the market was chaotic, generally ranging from $1,077 to $80. There were still 4,438 forward contracts remaining for this month.

Trading in the market was not active. In summary, Hengxing, Wanxing, Yufeng Yong, Yuanshengyong, Bingxing, Hengyu, Yuanmao, Yifeng Yong, Yuanmao Yong, Zhaofeng Factory, Yuanchun, and Dadecheng were on the selling side, while Hongli, Hengtai, Daxing Yong, Dakang Yong, Fengda, Changxiang, Shunli, Chunyuanyong, and Ruixing were on the buying side. Ruixing, Dadecheng, and Hengxing went out first and then advanced. Zhaofeng Chang and Yuanmao Yong advanced first and then went out. Dalian Banks and Shunli jointly traded over 2,400 forward contracts, netting over 200. Wanxing jointly traded about 2,200, netting out over 600. Guang Banks and Hengxing sold over 800 forward contracts, advancing just over 200. In addition, speculator Wu first sold and then slightly advanced, and Western merchants also made supplies. The total number of January tokens was 33,194.

American Exchange Rates Tighten by Half a Yuan Both Officially and Unofficially - Chinese Merchants and Sassoon Actively Buy In -

Yesterday, according to foreign dispatches, London forward contracts mostly rose by 1.125, American banks contracted by 3.375, the forward silver price fell by 6.5%, the British to American rate fell by 6.75, the American to British rate contracted by 8.625, the American to French rate fell by 7, the British to French rate contracted by 3.4, London spot gold rose six pence, the private silver price fell by 0.625, and exchange rates contracted by 7.75. The exchange market opened in the morning with recent selling prices of British exchange at one shilling three and a half pence and US exchange at $33.125, higher than the previous close by 0.0625 for British and 0.625 for American. Banks opened by selling, but Sassoon & Co. made some purchases. When the HSBC exchange rate was announced, American rates were reduced by half a yuan, French rates fell by two francs, and the rest remained unchanged. Later, the market went from flat to loose due to unfavorable foreign news. At noon, the market gradually stabilized. Later market trading was scarce, and the process was calm. The closing recent selling prices were British exchange at one shilling three and five-sixteenths pence and US exchange at $33.25, higher than the previous close by flat for British and tight by half a yuan for American. Banks sold out in large quantities, sometimes trading in Japanese-American exchange rates. Chinese merchants bought in about 400,000 to 500,000 yuan. Sassoon & Co. also bought in and simultaneously took in shillings. The day's transactions are recorded as follows:

British exchange opened in the morning with a recent selling price of one shilling three and a half pence. Citibank sold twelve and a half six-cent pieces to Zhengjin for the second half of December. The noon close had a recent selling price of one shilling three and five-sixteenths pence. Later, Zhengjin and Huabi sold sixty-eight and three-quarter pieces to Sassoon for February. The closing selling price ranged from one shilling three and five-sixteenths pence to eight and one-eighth pence, with the buying price increased by six-hundredths and twenty-five thousandths.

American exchange opened in the morning with a recent selling price of $33.125. Zhengjin sold March at $34 and April at $3.125. Shanghai, Huabi, Zhejiang, and Zhengjin sold to Sassoon March at $34. Huabi issued to Huayi April at $2.25. Huabi and Meifeng sold March at $34. Mitsui took in April at $3.125. Huabi continuously sold March at 0.0625. Mitsui bought March at 1.125. Overseas Chinese and Zhengjin sold March at 1.125. Banken sold March at 1.125. McCallie sold April at 3.375 to HSBC. HSBC traded Japanese-American exchange rates. Mitsui ate April at 3.375. Banken sold half a yuan for January to Citibank, Zhengjin, and McCallie, who also took it in. The noon close had a recent selling price of $33.25. Later, Sumitomo sold, while Shanghai bought April at 3.375 (Shanghai hedged Japanese-American exchange rates). Shanghai sold February at 8.125, selling April at 3.375 to HSBC. Zhejiang sold the same month and the same price to Zhengjin. Zhengjin sold February at 8.125 and March at 0.0625. McCallie sold March at 0.0625. The closing selling price was $33.25 for December, half a yuan for January, 8.125 for February, $34.0625 for March, and $3.125 for April, with the buying price increased by six-hundredths and twenty-five thousandths.

For francs, McCallie sold March at 540 francs, and Oriental sold January at 542 francs. McCallie sold February at 543 francs.

Large Forward Contracts Contract by 1.125

A National News Agency dispatch from London on the 12th: Large forward contracts recently at 18.5 pence, forward at 18 and five-sixteenths pence, each down 1.125 from the previous day. Also, the British-American exchange rate opened at $5.105.

Foreign Call Money Reopens at a High Price of One Dime

Since the abolition of silver in Shanghai's financial circles, foreign call money has been traded daily. Since the commencement of trading, this foreign call money has never reached a few cents, and any amount exceeding one dime has mostly been a flash in the pan, with no lasting duration. It had previously risen above one dime a few days ago but then fell back, standing at a few cents again. Yesterday morning and afternoon, it reopened at a high price of one dime. It is hoped that there will be a slight turnaround in the future. The "劃頭" was also drawn in white without adding water. Call money ticket trading: over 4.9 million transferred in the morning market, over 600,000 in new transactions, over 400,000 in the afternoon market, over 500,000 in transactions in the Small General Association, over 600,000 in foreign collateral withdrawals, over 1.1 million in new deals, over 800,000 banknotes in and out withdrawn, over 1.4 million issued, 100,000 from customer sources, 150,000 outgoing. Bank collections and payments: foreign banks collected and paid ticket money and silver over 2.7 million, foreign currency over 3.56 million, all kinds of goods, exchange, mortgage, and miscellaneous collections and payments silver over 4.67 million, foreign currency over 5.45 million, special collections and payments silver over 2.1 million, silver released from warehouse 500,000, foreign currency 600,000. Chinese banks collected and paid ticket money over 3.2 million, special collections and payments foreign currency over 2.4 million, all kinds of goods, exchange, tax, mortgage, and miscellaneous collections and payments over 5.6 million, silver released from warehouse 500,000. Japanese banks silver into warehouse 400,000, foreign currency 300,000. Money shops foreign public single collections and payments over 49 million, foreign "劃頭" collections and payments over 7.3 million, all kinds of exchange money over 600,000, cash collected 700,000. Also, the total number of exchanges in the local bill clearing house on the 12th was 5,763,907.74 silver dollars, including 2,456,621.42 silver dollars and 3,307,286.32 silver dollars in exchange transfers.
